      \n Let's see... They open the door to the third cell, and Bulat warns that this one holds ne'er do well street thugs. Some minor kerfluffle ensues when one of the "crows" tries to get in their faces, but Arselan and Niff are sufficiently intimidating (Arselan success on a Leadership roll) to convince them to submit to being tied in a coffle with their hands bound. Arian (partial success) uses Survival to do the tying, and with a few glares and idle threats toward Brog, whom these three thugs seem to know, the party exits the dungeon.

      They make their way through the hallways, seeing no sign of cultists, finally exiting the ground floor through a door onto a narrow paved street. By narrow, it's basically a bit wider than a single lane road.

      It is the middle of the night, dark as hell except for the single torch the party still has, and Sklarah's candle cantrip. The buildings on either side are about two stories high. There's a small fountain in the middle of the street a short distance away, just visible in the torchlight. As the party stands on the street, discussing where to go from here, Niff (failure on Awareness) senses movement on the rooftops, but not in time to warn anyone. There's a bit of a distraction as one of the Crows slips his bonds and tries to escape, but Arian and Arselan brace him before he can get away.

      Then the arrows and bolts fall on them as the remaining score of cultists let loose. Chaos breaks out. Everyone leaps this way and that, trying to get safe. The cultists turn out to be lousy shots. The Crows bug out, two of them taking minor wounds from arrows. Nunk is hit, to everyone's chagrin. Arselan gets his shield up to protect Nunk. Arian draws the bow she borrowed from Niff and picks off a cultist with a well-placed arrow. Lucius the Cleric (NPC today) is hit, and drops the torch. Sklarah (also an NPC today) douses her candle flame and ducks back inside the door. Niff puts on the defective owl goggles that grant Darkvision Only in Total Darkness. Thus equipped, he heads for the meager cover of the fountain and pulls a lightning gun. Andromeda goes to the near wall and prepares to climb it to get to the cultists on the roof. Valavanora moves toward the opposite wall and prepares to call on one of her spirits. Bulat takes an arrow but isn't hurt. Arselan takes a couple of arrows, but his armor prevents him from taking serious damage.

      I was pretty surprised the first round didn't scuttle a whole bunch of HP, but the characters rolled well. I haven't imposed penalties yet. That may happen in future for killing grounds, but there wasn't a need here as it was pretty exciting, and everyone felt threatened.

      Next round: Andromeda (success) climbs the wall and arrives at the roof's edge with her assassin's dagger. She promptly (partial success) shanks one of the cultists, but the second one freaks and clubs her with his crossbow. I was going to have her teeter on the edge, Dazed, but A suggests the blow knocks Andromeda unconscious so she plummets into the street. "You sure?" I ask. "Yes!" she replies. Yowza. Awesome Point!

      Meanwhile, Niff (partial success) uses his lightning gun to blow a cultist to paradise in Klassh'Tuu's fanged gut, but sees they're pulling up a freakin' wide-bore cannon to point into the alley. He correctly deduces this is a blunderbuss thing, full of scrap and shrap, and a cultist behind it holds a smouldering match. The rest of the cultists are preparing to fire again, cocking their crossbows. This round's arrow fire goes (die of FATE) primarily toward the bewildered and hurt Nunk, who takes about five hits while Brog cowers behind him and screams he's not with these people, he's not one of them!

      Motivation spikes among the group: these cultists must pay for this! M expresses the plaintive hope that Nunk doesn't die.

      Arian (partial success) throws herself under the falling Andromeda and catches her, but is hammered to the ground by the impact, taking some HP damage. Valavanora, in the middle of the street, summons her fiery phoenix spirit Koriander, who arrives in purple flame. Niff is immediately blinded and pushes the goggles up onto his forehead. He decides against trying a lightning gun shot at the cannoneer for fear of setting off the powder. Instead, he races to that wall and (success) climbs up, grabs a cultist and jerks the hapless sod caterwauling to the street.

      The cultists are getting ready to shoot, but Valavanora (success) orders Koriander to burn all the bowstrings, which I thought a brilliant tactic. Streaking like a purple comet, the spirit immediately turns all the bowstrings to ashes...starting with Arian's. Yeah, it was a success, but I figured EM needed a little cautionary note about taking care with spirit instruction. Plus the cultists are now effectively neutered...except for the cannon.

      Arian pushes herself up, pulls a lightning gun, and fires at the cannoneer, taking the shot Niff didn't. Failure! The bolt arcs right into the cannon's bore and there's a clap of thunder as the cannon discharges in an explosion! Shrapnel lashes the street, dealing damage to basically everyone. Valavanora (failure) collapses, still too close to Death as she hits 0 HP. The well-armored Arselan (success)shrugs off most of the shrap that comes his way, and immediately runs out to try to heal Valavanora. Arian (partial failure) evades damage, but suffers a scar.

      This was funny. I suggested a cool facial scar, and the girls all sat up straight, shaking their heads. Not in the face! They start talking about maybe a shoulder scar or collarbone scar that looks cool but can be concealed. I suggest Arian could lose an eye, which would be interesting, and M starts to think about that, with some misgivings. A offers the idea that maybe Arian could get a cool cat eye replacement, and she starts to warm to the idea of a Ranger with an eyepatch.

      The cultists flee in the face of all this table-turning. Niff (success) draws his sword and stabs one through the heart. Arselan (success) heals Valavanora, as his goddess decides the heathen druid has acted honorably enough today. G's comment is, "Yeah, yeah. Honor. I get it." I can't wait for the goddess to buff the Paladin when he acts in the name of honor, but right now it's clear the goddess is a bit on the judgmental side. Nunk the pincushion lives, but barely. He's in need of arrow-pulling and healing. Nobody is happy to see Brog crawl out unharmed. Bulat is OK too, having slipped to the side and healed himself, though he's still weak.

      That's pretty much where we left off. M's mom arrived, and M greets her with "I might have lost an eye! I haven't decided yet!" Then my wife shows up, and when she asks if anyone died, she's told "EM died again!" Valavanora hadn't died, not quite. But 0 HP is close enough to count, I guess. There's a lot of excited chatter and talk about what to do with Nunk and what they're going to buy when they go shopping again.

      EM decided she wants her Death Aspect to be a sort of Winter tell, with the touch of her hands leaving frost trails. Thanks to the Story Games Names Project and Shreyas for that idea, by the way. Pretty sweet.

      Next time, we'll see how and where they want to go in the wide World of Dungeons. Their backstories are pretty cool, I have to say. I'll have a metric ton of material to work with.

      \n That's true.

      CONDITIONS. I assign a Condition as a consequence. They're a nice alternative to HP loss, especially where the circumstances point toward a non-damaging result. I use them as soft moves if they're of very short duration, like when a player becomes momentarily Blinded. For hard moves, they work great for longer-lasting penalties. The restriction is either really clear from the fiction (e.g., Blinded) or I might assign a penalty of -1 or maaaaybe -2 depending on the severity of the fictional context. I also might just ramp up the fictional consequences of a miss (essentially what you reminded me is another axis to work on). I have told players that the particular Condition meant no modifier to the die roll, but would make failure way more complicated. As I think about it, that's my preferred method: to use Conditions less as mechanical modifiers and more as modifiers of the fictional stakes.

      I started out with a list of a dozen Conditions, and the players came up with a bunch more, so now I have the basic set and a bunch of blank ones on the character sheets. Live and learn.

      \n
      Second, I'm not sure if the "open your mind to the otherworld" is too powerful. I can make Amber's first debility severe, but if it's super cool, will that still leave wizards fairly unlimited? If we were dealing with older players, I wouldn't hesitate, but the young ones might not care for "your right arm turns to willow wood" or "sunlight burns an exquisite calligraphy of pain into your exposed skin." But maybe JM would love this stuff, who knows?
      \nYeah, you don't want to make it too harsh, but equally if it's not harsh enough (or if she thinks the consequences are cool) then it becomes a practically unlimited resource.

      I found the end of this DKids encounter really interesting and I think there's some potential mileage in playing the old 'with great power comes great responsibility' card. If JM learns that when Amber opens her mind that there are always unforeseen consequences then it'll naturally make her more cautious about using it as she won't know what the true cost will be. For example:
      - bargaining with the stone spirit - the first thing this says to me is that Amber is racking up obligations; she's going to have to ensure this citadel's destroyed now. And what is she doesn't? What will the consequences be from the stone spirit? Will they refuse to obey her in the future? Will they exact some greater retribution?

      - summoning a star spirit - I love that she thought of this, and it has huge Dark Phoenix-like potential for consequences. I think of star spirits and I think of star gods: Immense; Unimaginable Power; Vastly Distant; Alien; Unknowable. I wonder why star spirits aren't summoned more often. What danger could they represent? Has Amber's actions brought the star closer to the world - causing climate change for example? Has it opened some kind of underworld bridge so that star spirits may start appearing even when not summoned? What are the star spirits' true intentions?

      So possibly the result of opening your mind too many times is that unexpected consequences occur from those actions. Stuff occurs that you realise you're responsible for and which the party then have to deal with - and which might then require a sacrifice of some kind to fix. So rather than have it leaving a disabling or dementing mark on the character, it could explicitly lead to great complications (and further adventures) which would then lead the player themselves to limit their use. (e.g. "Are you sure you want to fill that last section? Do you remember how hard it was to get the star spirits to leave the world alone?")

      Anyway, just some thoughts.

      \n
      \n So we left the Dungeon Kids last time with them on the mountain path below the Citadel. The frost worm plummeted into the depths in a plume of rubble and dust, as the hobgoblins crouched with their crossbows up on the battlement. The party had withdrawn around the bend, leaving a 25-foot gap in the already treacherous path leading to the citadel's heavy iron-bound gate, which was backed by a portcullis.

      It's cold, the sun has set, and the wind howls through the mountain night, almost putting out the party's single guttering torch. All the characters (except Ingor the Elf Archer, who enjoys the protection of his magical Resist Cold ring) shiver in the sudden chill that descends with nightfall. Will they retreat into the dungeon and hole up in the bugbear's quarters?

      No, they decide they want to stay outside and ponder an attack on the citadel. But how will they manage to take effective counsel while the cold bites ever deeper?

      Amber the Wizard decides to open her mind to the Otherworld again, this time to summon a Fire spirit. She thinks about summoning The Book of Ice to see if it can use its Cold domain to move the cold away from them, but concludes the spirit might not be terribly happy about working in the service of Warmth. So she (success) summons a salamander from the party's torch flame. It crawls onto the path before her, the wind whipping the red flames spilling off its lizardy form. "How shall I ssserve you, wizard?" it asks.

      Amber could Command it, but she's decided she likes bargaining, and wonders if Commanding spirits is mean. So she asks the salamander to make a fire to keep everyone warm. The salamander blinks and asks how it can do that without enough wood to burn. There follows some discussion with the bewildered spirit, but Amber asks if it can use the entire torch but burn in a way that keeps everyone warm throughout the night. The salamander (CHA partial success) agrees this is possible, but it would take much effort on its part to draw so much heat for so long out of such paltry fuel. What will the wizard do to make such an effort worthwhile?

      Amber answers she would be willing to render it a service, of course. What would the salamander like? It thinks a moment, then answers that it has always dreamed of burning something large and interesting of structure. If Amber will help it to consume such a thing at some point in the future, it would gladly provide warmth through the night from that torch. She agrees, and to seal the bargain, the salamander wishes to leave a mark upon her little finger.

      "Oh, like pinkie swearing," JM says.

      "Yes," I reply. "Exactly."

      So the salamander's fiery tongue whips out and coils for an instant around Amber's pinkie, searing a brand into her flesh for 1 HP. I tell JM the HP will heal only when she completes her bargain. The salamander has her take a splinter from the torch to cast into whatever she will allow him to burn in the future. Then he scuttles into the torch, which Romrama drops on the path, and a bonfire sized flame leaps up to warm the party.

      JM fills in a third point on Amber's pentagram.

      Next: A gap in the night, and much attendant skulking.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nDecember 2012 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n With the salamander providing warmth despite the mountain wind, Romrama decides to sleep. He promptly lies down with a cloak as his blanket and begins to snore. However, Rhavaniel and Mist decide to try to climb across the gap, screw the dark and cold and wind. Rhavaniel is clearly willing to embrace Death, S having heard how cool Valavanora's encounter with the Grim Reaper was over in the Dungeon Girls' side of the pool. Mist, at least, puts on her climbing claws and ties a rope around her waist. Ingor holds the rope.

      I tell them it's gonna be a Athletics CON test instead of DEX, because of the terrible conditions. Both characters have high DEX, so this gives them pause. I explain, "Hey, you guys can cross this sort of gap in your sleep, but the dark, the cold, and this chilly, damp wind? Yeah, it's how tough and determined you are in this case." I do give Mist a +1 for the climbing claws.

      J didn't show, incidentally, probably because I neglected to send out reminders this week.

      Rhavaniel (crit) crosses the gap easily, though it takes a little while. She immediately goes to Scout the citadel, and slips up to the stone wall by the massive gate. Here she can listen in on the hobgoblins, who are busy gambling and eating. She (partial success) overhears them talking about the very interesting topic of favorite foods. One of the hobs goes on about how he likes his Dwarf. "Fried in butter with turnips, or better yet, dowsed with oil and set afire so's he gets all crispy." I play this out with the voices, and the kids giggle and C growls as Romrama (very likely) has a bad dream moment or two. It's pretty fun, and I hoped to establish the hobs as bonafide Bad Guys. The hobs also speculate that the adventurers probably fell to their deaths with the frost worm. "Too bad about the dwarf," says the culinary one.

      Mist (failure) gets across, but at a cost. I start to describe how the rocks on the opposite ledge crumble under her hand, and she has to scramble to keep her grip without pulling Ingor to the brink. S pushes over a couple of Awesome Points to move things to a partial success. Instead of directly jeopardizing the party, I describe how the rocks clatter down and create a small landslide below, making a ruckus. A suspicous hobgoblin pokes his head up to have a look, and I have both JM and R make Stealth rolls.

      They (both crit) successfully elude the hobgoblin's scan, despite his night vision. Mist swings down below the lip of the precipice, secured by her claws. Rhavaniel simply flattens herself to the wall directly below the hobgoblin. The hobs are sufficiently lulled to decide there's really nothing out there. Maybe it was an adventurer falling to its death, they joke. Har-har-har.

      The kids are really motivated to get these guys now. They're mean!

      The other characters cross easily on the rope, held on either end by Ingor and Mist. Romrama makes a crit for his crossing, so he's over in a flash. Ingor, his player not being here, fills the role of utility NPC and stays behind to hold the rope, while Mist puts a rock on the other end to hold it down. The party approaches the citadel and takes council at the base of the wall.

      There's some chit-chat about what to do next. Rhavaniel is all about going solo, and it's clear S is begging for death so as to have Rhavaniel become cool. She's not inclined to cooperate. I tell them to go into another room and Make A Plan. None of this haphazard stuff. These are tough, mean hobgoblins, and they're not going to fool around. I must have been convincing, because the kids pelt off like puppies to JM's room. I pour myself another cup of tea while I wait.

      Their energy has been pretty good so far. I'd let them have over an hour of playtime before we started, and that seemed to get most (not all!) of their ya-yas out. But this little break would hopefully help as well. C had been trying to take S's socks off under the table, which was probably a result of Romrama not having much to do as of yet. This would change very soon, with much carnage as the result.

      Next: The final assault on the Citadel!
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nDecember 2012 \n edited December 2012
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n The kids returned with a Cunning Plan. Well, not so much on the cunning side. It was really a straightforward plan that let everyone do what they wanted: Rhavaniel would scale the wall to try to catch the hobgoblins off guard and create a diversion; Amber would summon a wood spirit to open the gate, then an iron spirit to deal with the portcullis; Romrama would ready his axe to unleash havoc upon the hobgoblins.

      It goes well at first. Rhavaniel (crit) scales the wall easily, finding lots of handholds and slipping over the top in utter silence. The two hobgoblins occuping the section of wall over the gate and between the towers don't notice a thing as she slides into the shadows of the tower door. Amber opens her mind and (partial success) summons the wood spirit within the door, albeit with much creaking and groaning as the wood shifts and shudders under the stirring spirit's .

      "Do you Command it?" I say, after describing the huge face pushing out of the wood, knotholes forming eyes, splintery lips splitting out of the layered planks with a sharp crack.

      "No, I like to bargain."

      Sure? Yes, she's sure.

      "What do you will, wizard?" the wood spirit groans though its heavy plank lips.

      Meanwhile, all this wood noise has alerted even these complacent hobs, so they go on alert. One leans over the gate to look down in horror. "The adventurers!" he bellows. "They're here! There's one, right down there!"

      He and his buddy proceed to crank their crossbows. At this point, Rhavaniel sighs, nocks an arrow to her bow, and proceeds to crit the bejabbers out of one, putting an arrow into his...

      "Eye, Daddy!" JM crows.

      "Yeah, oooh, the eye!" C chimes in.

      "Yeah," says S, a gleam in her own eye.

      OK, the hob pauses as if confused, starts to shake his finger in Rhavaniel's direction, snarls at her, then drops like a sack of oatmeal. The kids' attention has (finally) become really focused. They can smell the fictional blood. The second one continues to crank his crossbow harder. Rather than engage further, Rhavaniel backs through the door at her back into the tower.

      JM says S wants Rhavaniel to die, so she's pushing toward that. S herself comments that she's rolling too well, which she is. I have the kids roll into a round die tray in the middle of the table, partly to keep dice results from going all over hell and gone, but also to encourage suspense and transparency.

      Romrama has his fighting spirits up and is ready to put the axe to some hobs. He (crit) climbs the wall himself, surprising everyone with his agility. Because it's a crit, I let him make a roll at the top to see if he can grab the other hob and hurl him off the wall. He (success) does, though at first C wants to seize him by the throat and strangle him, but after I tell him that might take a few rounds, he decides to go with the hob toss. Because he rolls a success, he doesn't drop the monster on Amber's head.

      Amber has been busy negotiating with the wood spirit. It says it wants to be alive again, so it will serve if she will take a shard and plant it in a mighty forest far from the horror of axes and saws. She suggests the Druid Lands, and the spirit agrees enthusiastically, drawing aside the reinforced gate like a curtain. Amber opens her mind a fifth time and (crit) summons the iron spirit of the portcullis. This one doesn't need much persuading. It wants to be left alone and not hauled up and down anymore, so it simply rattles and snakes open a hole big enough for Amber, Mist, and Lostariel to step through.

      JM was definitely more focused on Amber this session, which was actually cool. Likewise, S was more into Rhavaniel, so this made things a lot easier for me to run.

      The trio enters the grounds, and are immediately confronted with a half dozen hobs, some of them still struggling to put on their helmets and arm themselves. One races toward a smaller building off to the side, a key in his hand. Another is bawling orders to shoot these intruders right damn now! The key-wielding hob reaches a big door and jams the key into a hole, preparing to turn it and release what I have decided is a big troll, the classic Gygaxian regenerating kind (which I play like its inspiration, the troll from Poul Anderson's Three Hearts and Three Lions). The three guards in Tower One prepare to fight, while the lone hob on Tower Two grabs its weapons and charges down the stairs to where Rhavaniel lurks.

      Romrama surges up the stairs of Tower One, screaming dwarvish battle cries. The three hobs decide to gang up on him and as the Imperial Dwarf reaches the top of the tower, they yell and charge!

      Meanwhile, Rhavaniel pulls her dagger and tries to gut the hob rushing down the stairs, but (failure) gets shield rushed instead, and is slammed hard into a wall, which imposes the Dazed condition on her. S has a little smile on her face. Failure at last!

      Next: The Thing Behind the Door, hobgoblin havoc, and a hostage!

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nDecember 2012 \n edited December 2012
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Amber is Dazed from too much Otherworldly exposure. She reels over to lean against the nearest wall. Lostariel blends into the shadows and makes her way toward the hob with the key in the mysterious door. Mist unsheathes her Elven Sword of Tirandel and it (success) flares with wrathful blue light, Causing Fear in Orc-kind.

      The attacking hobgoblins freeze in their tracks, dumbstruck. The one with the key starts to panic, but redoubles his attempt to open the lock, terror making him clumsy and delaying him.

      Mist assumes an intimidating stance and (success on a CHA roll despite her CHA of 0) routs the hobgoblins. They turn and run, stripping armor and dropping weapons as they go, heading back into the keep and the secret passage to the dungeon below. The one continues to twist the key frantically. The door shudders as something big strikes it from inside, and a deep voice says, "Hooo."

      But the hobgoblins on and in the tower aren't affected by the Sword of Tirendel, because they can't see it. C describes how Romrama drops his shield and leaps amid the hobgoblins, axe held in a two-handed grip, and makes a whirling strike to hit all three. I decide to deal with this like the Cleave feat from 3E. Romrama (success) beheads the first outright, earning a roll against the second, which he also succeeds at with enough damage to kill it, thereby gaining a shot at the third. Here, a partial success means it takes half damage. But S pushes over an Awesome Point to bring Romrama up to a full success. It's not enough to kill the hob, though, so I describe how Romrama's axe shatters the hobgoblin's shield and deals a mighty wound to its arm. The wounded hobgoblin staggers back against the parapet, its arm hanging useless. It throws away its meat-cleaver sword and cowers, begging for mercy.

      "I will serve you, Dwarf-Lord! I will be your slave!"

      Romrama thinks it'll be cool to have a hobgoblin slave. "I accept," he says, "but I won't treat you as bad as a slave."

      "Thank you, Lord!" the hobgoblin cringes closer. "Thank you!" And then... as it gets even closer, Romrama (failure) suspects nothing. The treacherous hob leaps up with a shriek to bury a dagger in the dwarf's chest! It rolls 2d6 for damage and scores an 11! After subtracting his Tough and Armor, Romrama is down to 5 HP, with the dagger still in him and the parapet pressing at his back!

      Aha, I say in my best dramatic voice. The hobgoblin pushes you, snarling in your face, spit spraying from its fanged mouth as it tries to twist the knife deeper and finish you. Or push you to your death, 'cause it's not picky. Romrama (CON success) manages to retain his grip on his axe despite the pain, and rears back to take a mighty swing. The axe crashes into the hob's shoulder! It hisses, "How I hates you dwarfy scum..." and expires. He heaves the body over the wall. There follows a distant crunch as it hits the stony ground below. A disgusted Romrama pulls out the dagger and throws it aside.

      Meanwhile, Rhavaniel emerges from her Dazed state to find herself at the base of the tower, arm twisted up behind her, a dagger at her throat. A shaky voice growls in her ear, "Move, little elf scum. Maybe you'll live, maybe you won't. It's up to your friends."

      Next: Finale.
      \n

      \n

      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nDecember 2012 \n edited December 2012
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n In the courtyard, Lostariel throws a dagger at the hobgoblin with the key, but (partial failure) only wounds him badly. Screaming in pain and terror, he flees, leaving the key in the door. But to the horror of the characters, there's another impact, and a loud clack as the lock jolts the rest of the way open. The door begins to swing out! Forgetting the escaping hobgoblin, Mist and Lostariel race to the door and throw themselves against it to prevent whatever is inside from escaping. I use the success counting rules RobbMcDiarmid suggested above, and (die of FATE) determine the Troll is really strong and will require six successes to contain. The kids roll 1 success between them, Mist with 1 and Lostariel with 0, but then spend a boatload of Awesome Points to get Lostariel up to 3 successes, still two shy. The door begins to open, and I describe how Mist and Lostariel feel their boots slide over the rough stone of the courtyard. Immense green fingers with long black nails wrap around the edge of the door.

      JM remembers that Mist is now LUCKY! She rerolls, gets a success, and throws more Awesome Points to boost it to a crit for 3 more successes. I narrate how she uses the Sword of Tirendel to slash the knuckles of the green hand. With a "Hooo," the fingers are pulled back, and there's a moment's opportunity where they can redouble their efforts and slam the door closed. Mist, assisted by her gauntlets of DEX, quickly grabs the key and locks the door. Everybody sighs in relief.

      The last hobgoblin drags Rhavaniel out, trying to reach the keep. He shouts for her companions to keep their distance or he'll kill the elf. An outraged Romrama runs down the stairs, axe in hand. The other players back off. Rhavaniel bravely says in a small voice, "Don't listen to him. Don't let him get away."

      The hob passes the mysterious door with his hostage, and here is where Lostariel (success) has been hiding in the shadows. She leaps out to Backstab him, but (failure) misses her deadly strike, as the outraged hobgoblin jerks Rhavaniel around, his dagger doing a few HP damage to her as a warning. "Don't!" he cries. "Don't touch me!" Lostariel gets out of the way of his wild swing, but retreats until the hobgoblin resumes his trek.

      When the hobgoblin has gotten halfway across the courtyard, Mist raises her elven sword and makes a threat: "Let her go or else." The sword's baleful blue light (partial success) Causes Fear and the hobgoblin slashes wildly at Rhavaniel, doing lots of HP damage before he wheels and runs like a rabbit. Romrama (failure) isn't fast enough to catch up and the hobgoblin reaches the door of the keep. But Romrama asks if he can throw his axe.

      Sure he can. And he (partial success) nails the hobgoblin between the shoulder blades. The hob makes the classic three more steps before collapsing. Victory! Though Romrama's axe head is cracked from all the heavy armor-cutting it's been doing.

      "Can I buy a new one?" he asks, not too worried as he digests his lack of the traditional dwarven weapon.

      "Yeah," I say.

      "How far to the market from here? Can we go now?"

      "Not quite."

      I remind them that Rhavaniel is below zero HP, which means she's dying. Mist runs to heal her--actually she starts for Romrama first, since S has been saying she wants to die. I mention that one of Mist's friends is *dying* and might need attention first. Mist (crit) swiftly manages to stop the bleeding and hopefully save her companion. Rhavaniel (fails to Defy Death) returns from the Gate of Death with 1HP and bearing the mark of Death in some fashion.

      JM is psyched to have a magical mutation, but doesn't want it to be something she doesn't like, such as snakes for hair (one of the things I mention). S is delighted she's been Dead, and proudly announces it to her sister (A, the Necromancer) and mom when they arrive to pick her up. I caution them that the first mark or tell might be subtle, but repeated instances may result in things they don't like quite as much. S leaves considering whether her eyes should now be dead black as her Death-mark, or milky white. JM likes the idea of Amber's hair stirring perpetually as if blown by a phantom breeze. C is happy to have axe-blasted a bunch of bad guys, and his gramma thanks me for "doing this for the kids." I'm feeling good. We'd started late, but got a good jolt of gaming in during the two hours, fifteen minutes we've been at it.

      JM decides Amber's going to take it easy and use quicksilver more in future and not just run up the star. She's further decided to focus on Amber for awhile and let Mist go into the background for the time being. S will do the same with Lostariel. Next session we'll be at one character apiece. I feel like everyone got what they wanted this session--including me.

      \n Christopher, they don't right now. When we started Faery's Tale and World of Dungeons, it was Elder Moppet, Junior Moppet, A, and S. That went OK, but the older girls had a different agenda than the younger ones. Also, JM has a distinctly narration-heavy style of describing her actions (though she's gotten more terse with experience) that triggered the older girls because it seemed to bog things down. So right now the arrangement is that if we don't have an away playdate arranged for JM, she hangs back in the TV room and reads or draws or something. If EM doesn't have a visit arranged elsewhere, she does her own thing. At some point, I have a vision of an epic dungeon session with both groups and two DMs, maybe a climactic fight with a Big Bad.

      Thanks, Paul. I'm definitely learning how best to mesh rolls and the fiction.

      Other house rules that are emerging:

      SPIRIT TELLS. If a wizard fills the five-point star on the character sheet from opening to the Otherworld as a summoning method (and maybe different types of mage play different versions of magical Hangman), he or she gains a Spirit Tell, a magical mutation or consequence. Early tells are minor and relatively subtle, but if a mage keeps accumulating them, they become more drastic, even draconian. If the process continues long enough, the magic user may even become a spirit and could be removed from play. (This last bit is ripped from BW's Magic Burner.)

      SPIRIT LIKES. Spirits have innate things they like based on their domains and how they're used in play. For example, a Fire spirit commonly likes to burn things. A spirit is predisposed to do something it likes, and willingly makes bargains toward that end. If a spirit is summoned and successfully used for certain tasks often enough, it may gain a liking for that task, in which case it gets a extra die of effect bonus when asked to do that thing. This is a way for longtime spirits to evolve both personality and distinctive spirit skills over time. One of the reasons I like this is because if you use a spirit for negative tasks, like killing people, it starts to like doing that and will bend itself toward doing more, which could lead to interesting problems. It sort of builds in karma for how you use your magic, and makes Necromancers even scarier depending on what they do.

      \n Noofy, that would rock. Thanks, I'm glad you're enjoying it. It's super fun to write.

      John: a fuller version of the game? Hell yes, please include whatever bargaining mechanics you find here. And for that matter, feel free to grab whatever I post here for whatever you need: examples of play, house rules, etc. Thanks.       ...destruction of the world...
      \nMust have been quite a game.

      The Awesome Points made quite a difference in the DK game. Both groups immediately gravitated toward using them as a pool despite earning them and controlling them individually. There's little to no hoarding, and everyone freely offers Awesome Points to each other. I tried the fan mail bit, and I'm not sure that works as well with the younger crowd, since they just started handing over the fan mail chips as Awesome Points (which makes sense). On the other hand, that's not really a problem. We had plenty of hazard in both games, so it wasn't like the Awesome Points threw things off.

      Without the Awesome Points, both games would likely be much more gritty.

      \n\nDecember 2012 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Thanks, Noofy. Now I can't stop thinking about the Kyle Ferrin images either!

      As the DG get up to speed on the Obsidian Portal site, they're essentially making their own Bonds via backstory connections among the characters. For instance, Andromeda's uber-Necromancer father appears to be the candidate for Dark Boss, and he was responsible for the death of Valavanora's character, while Arselan's paladin Order has the task of monitoring the daughter (Andromeda).

      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nDecember 2012 \n edited December 2012
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Hey, so I have another AP to post. In the meantime, I reworked some new, expanded WoD character sheets to reflect feedback and my observations of the challenges the Dungeon Girls and Kids are encountering. They've hit some organizational snags in keeping track of all their kewl new abilities, loot, magical items, spirits, spirit marks, allies, etc. John Harper has kindly given his blessing for me to share the sheets with y'all. Feedback is welcome.

      And these were made on Pages, FWIW. I'm still in the process of learning InDesign, et. al. There's a lot of power and potential there, but the interface is obtuse as hell. When I'm shagging out something quick, I get lazy and drop back into Pages or OmniGraffle.

      Also, yeah, I'm using a shit-ton of different fonts, I know. Not best typographical practice. Send the design enforcer over to take a finger joint.

    [World of Dungeons] Dungeon Girls!

    \n
    \xab123456\xbb

    Comments

      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Whew. Two DG sessions to catch up on.

      One: Out of the Dungeon at Last!

      When we last left the Dungeon Girls, they had just survived an ambush by the remaining cultists of Klaash'Tuu. The players for Niff and Sklarah couldn't make it, so we had A, G, M, and Elder Moppet.

      It is the middle of the night, and though most of them have come through and been healed, their friend and charge Nunk lies bleeding from a half dozen arrow wounds. The group immediately starts stressing over him, expressing the hope he won't die.

      Rolls by the cleric Lucius and by Arselan the Paladin (partial successes) stabilize Nunk but not enough to save him, just buy time. After a quick discussion, they decide Arian the Ranger and her lion Hodori will race ahead to the inn and get help. Meanwhile, the rest of the group will carry Nunk to the inn.

      Arian (partial success on Survival) finds the way to the Inn successfully, though doing so takes her longer than anticipated because the city is pitch dark and its streets unfamiliar. Once there, she (partial success on a CHA roll) discovers the innkeepers (it's a high class place) will certainly call for a doctor who lived nearby, but won't risk its people venturing deeper into the dangerous city at night.

      Meanwhile, Niff and Arselan attempt to carry Nunk to the inn, but (failure on CON roll) find out he is too heavy and everyone too wiped out to bear him much more than halfway. Nunk lies in the street while the party catches its breath and tries to figure out how to get the big guy the rest of the way.

      Valavanora decides to summon an air spirit to make Nunk lighter. After some discussion, she (crit!) summons a spirit with the Domains Wind and Burdens. It manifests as a cricket formed of softly shifting sand, and she decides its name is Bercalion, the Desert Breeze at the Back That Eases Burdens. She doesn't have Command, so she bargains with it, helped by the critical success. She appeals to its better nature, stressing how she wants to help a friend. She (critical CHA roll) impresses the spirit with her kind heart, and it replies that it has been long since a human has called upon it to assist in an act of mercy. Not only will it grant her petition to lighten the burden of Nunk, but it would be willing to travel with Valavanora as her ally if she would pact with it. She agrees, and the spirit dissolves into a sandy breeze, and swirls up her forearm, its sand particles scratching a graceful spiraling mark of fine, pale lines upon her skin for 1HP to seal the agreement. The marks glitter faintly under light. Everyone is impressed, and Bercalion causes a breeze to blow that seems to make Nunk lighter and everyone refreshed enough to bear him all the way back to the inn.

      At this point, the non-magic user members of the party are starting to feel like also-rans. The mages are just SO COOL! M and G look a little crestfallen. I am sure the tide will turn when the group gets into a situation that leverages the talents of the others. M asks if non-mages can get spirit powers.

      I think about it a second and answer, "Sure. You can't summon or command spirits, but if you meet one and can bargain with it, you can make a pact and gain powers. Why not?"

      She seems reassured. I point out to G that Arselan could think of his goddess as a giant spirit he's already in a relationship with. He needs to build that relationship.

      I think they're reassured, anyway.

      Back at the inn, the doctor arrives, Nunk is treated, there's a brief talk about what to do next, and after seeing Nunk tucked into a feather bed stained with blood and grime from his dirt-encrusted body (to the innkeeper's delight), the party finally sleeps.

      Next: SHOPPING! and the dark rituals of summoning

      \n\nMathalus \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Just chiming in to say that I love this thread.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n In our first session, the party had gone to the great bazaar of the city of Shardeej, but except for Valavanora, nobody had any bank outside of the starting first level character budget. Now things were different, and the girls were eager to spend their hard-won silvers.

      The first thing they decided on was horses for their trip. They had some discussion about next steps and concluded after looking at the map that they wanted to head toward the Regency and the Druid Lands. (I'll get around to posting a scan of the initial map. I have plans to do it up in more detail and style.) G wanted to cross the inner sea toward Ankhyra, since Arselan's goddess Ceridwen was the Lady of Waters, and Andromeda wanted to go to Ankhyra as well, but the rest of the group argued for an overland route to the Regency. After some back and forth, they voted for overland, but with the compromise that they would travel along the coast.

      Hence the horses. Everyone was quite specific about what they wanted, and spent some time detailing their horses' appearance. I told Arselan he owned his own horse already, since he was a paladin, and a trained war horse at that. This was sort of a gimme, but I thought it reasonable given how much leadership G had shown, and I was looking for ways to show how the non-mage characters were awesome.

      So...the party proceeds to the bazaar, where they split up. I let the horse purchase happen off-stage without a roll, since each of the subgroups had different agendas, and I wanted to focus on those.

      Valavanora and Andromeda want fancy dresses, masterwork quality. I name a price basically twenty times that of a standard dress, and they each buy one with a little haggling but no roll. That meant Elder Moppet would (and did) spend a good deal of the session drawing and coloring her dress. I suggest pearls sewn into the silk, and EM enthusiastically agrees. A draws Andromeda's dress as well, which is much less flamboyant, as befits the necromancer daughter of one of the setting's big bads. They ooh and ahh over how awesome their fancy dresses are, and how they'll be able to use them to make CHA rolls at special parties and court events.

      M wants her ranger Arian to have a new bow, but a really good one. She decides her Level 3 Special Ability will be Volley instead of Wild. She really wants to talk to Hodori, but concludes that maximizing damage is more important at this stage. She asks about a composite bow, and I name a price ten times that of the heaviest bow in the equipment list. She (success on CHA) counterbids and gets the price lowered by over ten percent. Done. She happily describes her wood and horn bow, and I add some verbal filigree about decorative carving on the horn part so it has personality. We have some discussion about how she would carry it on her person along with sword and spear and quiver and so on.

      Haggling is fun.

      Next up, Arian and Arselan go to an alchemist's shop to sell a few of the lightning guns taken from the skitterlings. I make sure to describe the shop in some detail and introduce the shopkeeper as Kassai the Clever, Alchemist of the Fifth Star. These could go for a decent price, but the group only agreed to sell a few of the guns, since they have more guns than charge vials. After some haggling with Kassai, who points out that the guns alone are mere curiosities, but a working gun with a charge vial would command a much better price, they (crit) negotiate the sale of three guns and one half-full vial. I use the success accumulation rules for this exchange. Because of the crit, Kassai gives them a decent price and tells them to come to him first with such interesting things, as he would be their friend in future.

      Meanwhile, Andromeda and Valavanora go to an occult shop to purchase a special ritual dagger for Andromeda. This does not go well, as the shopkeeper (failure on CHA) recognizes Andromeda as a necromancer and immediately ejects her from the shop, refusing service.

      I should point out the girls have been using Awesome Points like crazy, so some of these successes and crits result from them throwing their points down to boost results. When the points are plentiful, they don't give this decision much thought. I expect them to be more parsimonious when they get thin. As I may have said before, I've been using plastic crystals (MTG mana trackers) to denote Awesome Points, and the group seems to enjoy them.

      Andromeda decides to summon a powerful spirit using ritual to empower one of her daggers into a magical item. After proceeding to a necropolis in the city, she uses Ritual to create a special summoning circle and what I take to be a containment circle for the dark spirit she wants to summon. She crits on the summoning roll (!) and gets a really powerful spirit whom she names Nagrasagiel the Judge. I draw upon the sheaves of random crap I've printed off from various oracles and generators and decide Nagrasagiel is a chief servant of one of the Gods of the Dead. So yeah, powerful as hell.

      Valavanora is watching from a (hopefully) safe distance.

      I describe how the scene goes gray, color drawing back from the area around the necromancer as the Judge manifests in the form of a gaunt man with pale skin and a stained gauze bandage over his eyes, clad in a ragged shroud with strips that ripple up around him in jagged patterns. The paving stones of the necropolis bend beneath his feet. I'm thinking a Brom moment here. His domains are Strength and The Dead.

      Negotiation commences. What is Andromeda willing to give up for the pact? This is a serious deal, as she describes what she wants for the dagger. She wants it to damage wraiths and the undead, and to give her some ability to protect the party other than melee capability. Truth be told, she doesn't have a super detailed picture of what she wants, but she's down for a cool story. I love it, and we bargain back and forth as the rest of the players chime in. Problem is, Nagrasagiel ain't no puny little spirit; he's a demigod. His ask is for something big and permanent, like an inability to lie or to feel love and affection. He says he'll grant power commensurate with what he takes.

      A decides Andromeda isn't willing to give up love, as it turns out. The players throw out suggestions and perch on the edge of their seats as A thinks about it. Finally, Andromeda decides.

      "My eye," she declares. "I will give my eye."

      I'm not rolling for this. Come on.

      "A fitting price for a judge," the spirit responds. Andromeda feels a terrible pain in her left eye and it's gone, leaving only a shadowy eye socket. The whole eye socket, mind you, like a freakin' skull. Filled with inexplicable darkness. The gray of the world around them retreats into the dagger, and Nagrasagiel points out that she can only use the dagger "to bring justice to the dead."

      Andromeda slumps to her knees as the spirit departs, leaving the dagger glinting blackly in the sunlight.

      The table is silent and appreciative for a moment, though A is beside herself with excitement. She immediately begins erasing her character picture to make the adjustment and then draws her long black hair so it falls dramatically over the socket.

      M says, "I can't believe you gave up your eye."

      I'm a bit amused at how the girls aren't into their characters sporting facial scars, but tearing out a whole eye is awesome. These girls are badass, fancy dresses and all.
      \n

      \n
      She crits on the summoning roll (!) and gets a really powerful spirit whom she names Nagrasagiel the Judge.
      \nThis is a relatively minor point in the overall awesomeness, but I want to call it out. Did she get that name from somewhere, or just come up with it all on her own? Because that's fantastic. Even if she didn't invent the name, it's still great to see that she has good taste in names and isn't just calling him "Bob". (Not that I think you'd let Bob stand as an appropriate name in this case.)
      \n

      \n
      \n

      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n

      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      Did she get that name from somewhere, or just come up with it all on her own? Because that's fantastic.
      \nThanks. I think it's fantastic too. :-)

      We have the Story Games Names book on hand as our name bible, and A chose it from there. She and all the DG have great taste in names. Honestly, one thing about this game is that I'm pulling in a ton of extra resources: the Names book, free maps downloaded from the net, dollar dungeons, oracles, the Harrow Deck, a random D&D treasure generator. But the Names book is our go-to for all things name-related. I've pushed John's WoD (WoDu) list from p.3 as well, and it's getting some traction, but all the kids think the Names book is the bomb. I should just graft a bookmark on the Elvish lists, because all the girls go there first. Maybe the Arthurian one as well.

      One thing I should mention: we do all our rolling in a die tray, a wooden candle holder I found at Goodwill. It's just a round, six-inch diameter, inch-deep tray, but it works great as a showcase for die rolls. I use it in my 1492 Other Worlds game too. It has the bonus of keeping dice on the table, esp. for the little ones. The Dungeon Kids have rolled outside the tray a few times, and the dice go all over the place.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n And here's the write-up of Thorn. I did this, embellishing on A's description of what she wanted. With this and another weapon coming up in the next write-ups, I started experimenting a bit, shamelessly ripping from the other awesome ideas folks are putting up in other threads. A did name the dagger herself.

      The dagger THORN has four powers granted to it by the Judge Nagrasagiel.

      1) It replaces one of the d6s the player normally uses. When wielded against the living or using it merely in self-defense, the player rolls a d4 (plus another d6) instead of 2d6. If it is used against the Dead with the intent of staying in the battle until the Dead are put to rest, the wielder rolls a d10. If it is wielded in a battle against Dead that are not put to rest (i.e., the wielder flees or the Dead escape), then the dagger user only rolls 2d4 with it until it is successfully used to put Dead to rest, at which time it resumes its former power. Its other powers will not function until it is \u201creconsecrated in judgment.\u201d

      2) Thorn grows cold in the presence of Undead.

      3) Thorn can strike any manner of Dead, Undead, or ghosts regardless of whether they are material.

      4) When the wielder sacrifices 1 HP of damage and uses the Turn Special Ability, Thorn adds +2 to the roll. This HP may not be healed until the next new moon. If the wielder does not possess the Turn special ability, she may invoke Nagrasagiel and sacrifice 1d6 HP to gain the ability for one immediate use. These HP may not be healed until the next new moon.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n

      \n Thanks, Noofy. I'm so digging the experience. The interesting thing about WoDu is how light it is, yet how substantial. Unfortunately, I don't know how long I can keep up the intensive blogging now that I've started a new job. I'm a couple of sessions behind as of today's Dungeon Kids throwdown.

      We haven't been using Playmobil for character figures, but that's a great idea. It's been more that when taking a break from WoDu play, the kids have gravitated to the Playmobil toys.

      Dyson's book? Am I missing something here?

      The overland map came from an initial collaboration with Elder and Junior Moppet, using John's page 3 name atlas for the major regions. I sketched out a coastline and placed mountains and rivers with input from the girls. JM "inked" my penciled features and colored the Druid Lands' forest and the Great Waterhole. As you might imagine, some of their input came with unexpected elements. For example, JM told me the Islands are all connected with stone bridges which we determined are more like massive walls sunk into the water. There's potential for the ruins of a huge undersea city there, but in the meantime, all the islands have foot and wagon commerce with each other, though sea trade would still be more economical. Also, there's an inland sea or mighty lake in the Great Desert that JM calls "The Great Waterhole," so I imagine tons of animals come there to drink, maybe under some sort of spirit-enforced peace. EM placed the Druid Lands between the Regency and the Northlands, and added some details about a huge waterfall coming off the eastern plateau. They named some cities as well, drawing inspiration from The Roman Mysteries, a series I've been reading to them.

      The Dungeon Girls didn't add to the map, but integrated it into their characters' backstories, so we discovered a little more about a few of the countries.

      \n Ah, thanks. That looks like an excellent resource. I will have to grab it tonight. I've been snagging a ton of stuff from DeviantArt and various gamer sites around the web. I'll try to get some photos up when I scan the map.

      Yes, those walls constitute a fantastic emergent detail. I have plans to refine the map and redraw it on a larger piece of parchment colored paper. From a sneaking-in-the-parenting standpoint, I used the map drawing session as a teaching opportunity and spoke to trade, geography, and settlement patterns.

      Speaking of emergent campaign details, the Dungeon Girls are starting to make their own plot as their backstories mesh, which is fine by me. I'll talk more about that as I catch up with that group's adventures.

      \nThe Prophecy
      As he took her eye, Nagrasagiel sent Andromeda a powerful vision of things yet to come. For this, I'd cribbed a ton of list material from Abulafia and strung it up with randomly generated villain concepts. The centerpiece was "the Merchant of Maggots," an image of a foxlike woman clad in fine, yet threadbare garb. I read through my list of stuff, checking off elements.

      The players seemed excited by the "prophecy," and G wrote it all down. There was stuff about a cliff of screaming monkeys, a golden armlet on the skeletal arm of its owner, a deadly assassin, a glowing skull holding the soul of a magician king, a raving prophet and soft-hearted shepherd. If any of you have played In a Wicked Age, you know the sort of thing I'm talking about. But for the girls, it was exciting and murky and ominous, exactly as intended.

      OK, so prophecy in a high fantasy milieu is an overused trope, but it feel fresh to the Dungeon Girls. What's cool about prophecy as game story delivery vector is that I can take the mosaic bits of imagery and weave them into the players' story as we go forward, connecting the bits of prophecy to the Fronts and Grim Portents.

      Right. So a weary Andromeda picks herself up, collects the newly empowered dagger Thorn, and she and Valavanora return to the inn. There they meet the rest of the group and she shares her vision. After some discussion, involving a lot of oohs and ahhs about the skeletal parts of the prophecy, they renew their resolve to travel toward the Druid Lands by way of the coast. The next morning they set off with horses and a mule. Nunk is too big to ride, so he's on foot but uncomplaining. He's happy the girls are willing to feed his prodigious appetite.

      Arian (critical success) leads them swiftly and safely through the desert for several days, having departed from the road for what looks like a more direct route through the desert and a range of hills toward the eastern end of the middle sea (name TBA). In the hills, they arrive at a rise over a canyon. There are the ruins of an old city there, pressed up against the base of the cliff. They see greenery, indicating water. And there appear to be lots of monkeys scampering up and down the cliff. The party can hear their shrieks from here.

      Several girls exclaim, "Monkeys..." A little thrill of anticipation passes through the group.

      In the distance, they make out gathering clouds that Arian (success) correctly recognizes as an approaching sandstorm.

      Next: Ruins in the Sand
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Arian will scout the city to see if it's inhabited before the group seeks shelter there. She and Hodari slip down to the sand-colored wall. She finds a gap in the wall and enters to find a string of camels, a small oasis in the remnants of an ancient courtyard. Someone says something in a guttural tongue. A tower is still intact, and she crouches in the shadow of the courtyard wall to observe. Rough-looking men in desert garb emerge from the tower to stand in the scant shade and give the camels some cursory attention. A couple make their way toward another mostly intact building closer to the cliff. Their speech is also rough, and Arian wonders if these guys are bandits. She scouts a little closer, (success) managing to remain undetected as she peers into the darkened interior of the tower. Around a dozen swarthy men sit around a small fire drinking what smells a little like coffee. She (success) sees the men are well-armed, but irregularly--everyone seems to have different gear, nothing standard, lots of weathered finery and patchwork robes. There's also a couple of chests in there, and one guy is kicking a bag that jingles as if with coin. The men laugh, but it's kind of a nasty laugh.

      Arian decides they're bad guys and retreats to the inside of the wall, where she (partial success) looses an arrow bearing a red strip of cloth in a high, fluttering arc as the prearranged signal for the party: danger here. Unfortunately, a bandit happens to look her way as she does this. He shouts. The alarm is raised!

      Next: Battle of the Sand Bandits!
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Meanwhile, and before the arrow comes up, Andromeda decides Arian has been taking too long, and she sneaks down the hill. The others wait, but Valavanora prepares to follow. Niff and Arselan stay back for now, out of sight behind the crest of the hill, but ready to charge in on horseback if necessary.

      Meanwhile, M decides Arian needs to get the hell out of there. Hodari snarls, which gives the first bandit pause, and Arian tells him to leap to the top of the wall. He does so reluctantly, while she puts an arrow into the bandit before slinging her bow onto her back and climbing the wall. At least, that's the plan. Unfortunately, a handhold (failure) crumbles under her grip, sending her tumbling onto the sandy courtyard floor, stunning her. Hodari roars and leaps down to stand over his friend as the bandits come running and draw up short when they see the...*cough* mightyferocious lion.

      Their courage returns as some of them arrive with bows and spears. While Arian groggily tries to regain her bearings, the bandits approach with death in their eyes. They're not shooting arrows until everyone is braced with their spears. Things look bad.

      Meanwhile, Andromeda has (success) gotten inside the wall undetected, sliding from shadow to shadow and hiding in the sparse shrubbery and one of the few palm trees there. She pulls a non-magical dagger which she (crit) uses to cut a passing bandit's throat from behind. Cue bloody arterial FX, I think, but A is ahead of me. For the additional cool crit bit, she asks if she can direct the spray of blood to blind the bandit's companion momentarily.

      Oh hellz yeah. +1 forward. She (success) knifes the poor blinded guy on the next round.

      Back at the cornered lion, things look bad. M is fretting Hodari will be hurt or killed. As he gathers himself to spring, the bandits brace their spears and a few take aim with a mix of bows, javelins, and crossbows.

      Valavanora, meanwhile, still approaching the wall, calls Koriander, who shows up in emerald flames. Having learned her lesson from the fight in the alley of Shardeej, Valavanora tells Koriander to ignite all the bandits' weapons. This the phoenix spirit (success) accomplishes in her usual spectacular fashion, and the bandits' missile weapons and wooden-shafted weapons burst into flame. So too do their metal weapons for a single round. But as the wooden weapons burn, the metal ones don't. Still, only a couple of bandits have the fortitude not to fling their swords and knives away. Those that don't are Dazed from the pain of their burned hands.

      Mind you, Koriander is swooshing through the courtyard, finding other weapons to burn. Crude racks of spears and bundles of arrows all turn to kindling in a few seconds. The effect roll is high enough to create a lot of chaos. After a moment, the bandits start picking up their cooling swords as they try to regroup. An enraged Hodari leaps into the midst of the ones threatening Arian. Gruesome bitey-clawy carnage commences. Andromeda (success) sticks another bandit in the confusion, but doesn't get an insta-kill.

      Up on the hill, Arselan and Niff and Sklarah (remember, neither L nor F are here, so it's just G) spot reinforcements emerging from the other building, a half-dozen men racing for the courtyard. G decides it's cavalry time. She and Niff thunder down the hill, the paladin's warhorse swiftly taking the lead as he raises his sword in the name of his goddess. Sklarah follows with the rest of the horses while Nunk lumbers in in their wake.

      A bloody rout follows. Arselan (success) immediately decapitates one of the reinforcements and rides down a second. The extra d6 of damage I grant for being on horseback versus infantry isn't remotely needed. NPC-for-the-day Niff takes out a guy himself, though with less panache. By this time, Arian rolls up into a crouch and (success) feathers an attacker right between the eyes. Valavanora arrives, bow at the ready, and picks off another. Andromeda kills her man, but takes a nasty cut. She flips back her hair to reveal her gaping eye socket, and (CHA success) intimidates the bejeezsus out of the five or six surviving bandits, who already aren't doing real well from a morale standpoint. Abject surrender follows. Arian calls Hodari off from his latest shrieking victim. All is quiet except for the groans and whimpers of wounded and dying bandits.

      But whoops, no time to celebrate. Sandstorm! The characters pool their ability rolls to get everything under cover in the tower, horses and all. Arian and Valavanora roll Survival, Arselan Leadership, and they (partial and full successes) score (die of Fate = 3) more than three successes to get everyone in...except Nunk.

      Pandemonium. Everyone starts to volunteer to head out to find him, but Valavanora takes the initiative. Andromeda holds a rope and makes her way out to the wall while Valavanora ventures out through the gap into the storm. She (crit bought with Awesome Points) manages to clasp hands with Nunk before the storm renders everything utterly opaque. They (success on CON roll) struggle back to safety, and everyone breathes a sigh of relief.

      The session pretty much ends there. We spend a few minutes handing out experience and loot. Valavanora levels to 4th, which puts her in the lead of all the characters thus far. I decided that since they didn't finish out the Temple of Klassh'Tuu, this would be a loot bonanza. Besides, I wanted to try out some of the magical item rules different folks have posted here.

      Valavanora takes a CON point for her Level bonus.

      Next: Abundant loot and a Thing of Power
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n

      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n As we go through the loot they find in the tower and in the outlying building, a few interesting items come to light: There's a cool +2 kite shield painted with a winged serpent emblem that Arselan turns down because it's not his style. There's a non-magical eyepatch embroidered with an eye in silver thread. Andromeda claims a longsword with Ghost Touch. A frog ring that grants a Great Jump skill three times a day goes to Arian. Potions and scrolls go primarily to Sklarah, who also receives a gnarled staff that seems to be connected to summoning woodland spirits. Once again I'm struck by how even-handed this group is.

      Let me pause to point out that I find myself blocked at times thinking of interesting things to award. For some reason, it's felt challenging for me to think up cool and interesting items. I found a website here that lets you generate random D&D treasures, and what's actually really cool about it is how it produces detailed non-magical item "art" objects. You have to hit refresh a bunch, but it's not bad as a starting point.

      Anyway, the eyepatch was one of these objets d'art, and other gewgaws like opal-studded hand mirrors and silver leaf-pattern rings were a big hit with the group, purely for the fashion possibilities. Any other group I've ever been in would have immediately assessed the value of this stuff for sale. Not the Dungeon Girls. They really appreciate these items. But my goal is to come up with interesting stuff that feels unique and has a place in this world's history, not just "+1 sword." I'm still figuring out the history details, but you get the idea.

      The site also kicks out colors, smells, and tastes for the potions, which is fun when it comes to potion investigation.

      Now, I'd been wanting to experiment. There was a coffer in a chest, accompanied by a heavy shortsword in a finely-wrought sheath. The hilt looked like it might be gold with a red leather grip. However, the pommel was a single giant garnet carved in the shape of a human skull.

      "I don't know," M says. "A skull seems pretty evil to me."

      A makes a noise about wanting it, but not too seriously. She'd already gotten the ghost touch sword and is perfectly happy with Thorn. EM is still coloring Valavanora's fancy dress. F wasn't there to argue for Niff, and Arselan doesn't think the skull motif fits Arselan's faith. They don't sense any obvious evil from the sword, though. When Arian gingerly draws the sword partway from its sheath, she sees the blade is the same pale gold as the hilt, but what looks like twin serpents entwined with each other along each side of the blade. These are rendered in black enamel.

      Ominous. Nobody is terribly enthusiastic about this weapon. But we have to table the rest for the next session. Everyone seems satisfied with the encounter with the bandits, though. Or maybe I should say satiated. Victory brings with it a certain bonhomie.

      Next: Interlude on the notion of "playing right"

      \n This thread is heinously miscategorized. It is the first thread I check.

      Moderators: I nominate this thread for Best of Story Games.
      \n

      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n

      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Dungeon Kids skipped a week due to New Year's, so Dungeon Girls (and Niff) assembled for their next session ready to finish the looting of the bandit encampment. Sklarah is in Washington with her family, so the DG are still not at full strength.

      While the other players were socializing among themselves G confided to me that she's struggling a little trying to find the right note for Arselan. She said she sometimes feels like Arselan is the noble good guy in a party of these shifty, maybe-evil necromancers, druids, and mercenaries, and she's worried he wouldn't really stay with them.

      I told her my first RPG character ever was a D&D Paladin in a party that turned out to be riddled with chaotic to chaotic evil behavior. Anyone who's ever played a paladin will recognize this quandary. I frequently had to play my guy as gullible or unobservant just to rationalize staying with the party. You could call that a basic expression of Author mode, I guess. But I told G that Arselan could frame his dilemma in different ways to justify sticking around without compromising his moral stance. She'd already established in tandem with A that Arselan's Order is responsible for containing the Big Bad Necromancer who is Andromeda's father. Also, his Chapter in particular had been tasked with monitoring Andromeda herself, the necromancer's daughter known only as the Black Rose.

      So Arselan staying with the group to keep an eye and possibly a sword on Andromeda was a good thing. G seemed happy with that.

      I'm struck by how the girls want to "play right." I'm trying to convey a vision of play that isn't about "getting it right" but about "bringing the awesome." Sure, there's some social contract pieces, and these include certain agreements that make the shared fiction seem plausible and therefore lend weight to the imagined space. But it's not about right or wrong. The writer in me wants to tell them to beat up their characters as much as possible and run them through a series of horrific wringers, because that's how you test your character and grow the depth.

      But I think they get that on an intuitive level. Each cool scar and death mark and spirit mark and so on makes their characters deeper and more interesting in a wabi-sabi manner. I haven't been able to mess with them much yet outside of tactical engagements, but as their backgrounds come more into focus, that'll happen. As I've mentioned, they have given me so much rich seed material, I can't wait to water it and see what grows.

      My God, their backstories are full of flags...!

      EM made the cautious comment to me after the session that she's "sort of more interested in our stories than in the Firejewel quest thing" I'd tossed out at the outset. Music to my ears. I'm sketching out some Fronts and Threats based on the background material the girls have put together. I will work the Firejewels in, but they won't be the heart of the quest.

      Next: The sword called Scourge -or- The Joy of Recycling Old Campaign Features
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n As we start this session, all these flag concepts are whirling around in my head: fancy dresses, horses with flowing manes, pets, orphan backstories, spirit marks, fighting a giant monster in the wilderness, cool scars, visiting the lands of the characters' childhoods, confronting Andromeda's evil big bad father...whew.

      They're going to need some firepower. Some of this the mages are building as they bind new spirits. But it's time for me to see what happens when I drop in something really powerful. I'm curious as to how the Dungeon Girls (& Niff) will react. Plus I want to test out some rules variations, push the boundaries a bit.

      So I built Scourge. Scourge was a magic sword I'd made when I was DM-ing D&D back in my high school days, when my peers and I roamed the primal pre-Internet earth with sabertooth tigers, mammoths, and 8-track tape players. The new iteration of Scourge looked about the same, if only to keep me from trying to keep Gene Wilder separate from Johnny Depp in my mind's eye. The original was built as a Stormbringer-style weapon that wanted to drive its owner toward mayhem and drinking blood, but I decided I wanted the reboot to be more targeted in its semi-antagonism.

      But I wanted it to be powerful, more so than the original. I wanted it to be the kind of item you wanted to wield, but also made you wary because it could bite you in the face if you were careless. The brilliant Soulbrand sword write-up done on the World of Dungeons Resource Compilation thread offered a good starting point. (Apologies for the lack of attribution, but I'm too lazy to go look up the post. But it was fantastic.)

      I was curious as to who would go for the sword. Because of the weapon's nature, the wielder would have to be Arselan, Niff, or Arian. Scourge, you see, was forged to be a mage-killer. I have some faux history to flesh out, but in the past, there was some kind of Wizard War that resulted in a massive effort to take down a huge order or alliance of magic users. I don't know why; maybe the wizards were tyrannizing the spirits, maybe there was some dark big-bad who built a dark bad empire with lots of orcses, maybe well-meaning magic users opened up a Pandora's Box that could only be closed with wizardly blood. But Scourge would be an artifact of that war, forged and fated to kill magic users.

      Here's what I came up with. I kept the write up to a page, typed it up, and got it ready as a handout. Feedback welcome, as always.

      SCOURGE
      DESCRIPTION
      Heavy Masterwork short sword of pale gold metal (orichalcum) with black serpents intertwined on the blade, a pommel of garnet worked in the form of a skull. Deals 2d6+STR damage, unbreakable by normal means.

      POWERS
      1) FATED WEAPON
      When a new owner picks up Scourge, you take a scarlet d6 and set it to \u201c1\u201d. Anytime you roll the dice while wielding Scourge, you can swap the scarlet die\u2019s current value for one of your dice (and that die\u2019s value becomes Scourge\u2019s new value).

      So if I roll a 4 and a 5 and get 9, I may want to downgrade to a 1 and a 5 and rely on my stat to pass the check (or my skill to keep from failing on a 6-). So you have to suffer a few setbacks to power Scourge up, but then you\u2019ll have a 5 or 6 stored in the sword, waiting for a crucial roll to use it.

      When the player is using Scourge to confront evil magic users and creatures of magic, use Scourge\u2019s die value for the die of fate for things related to the wielder without swapping it!

      2) DEADLY.
      When wielding Scourge, any 6\u2019s rolled to hit for for damage with the sword \u201cexplode,\u201d meaning you keep the six and reroll that die, adding the result to your total. If you swap the six out per FATED WEAPON, you do not reroll at that time, but may reroll at the time you swap in that six.

      3) MAGE KILLER.
      Deals +1 damage to any character who has a Special Ability from the Wizard class. When Scourge successfully deals the death-blow to a magic user, take +1 forward with the weapon until the next die swap per FATED WEAPON, above.

      4) AWAKENED SPIRIT.
      Unlike most magical items, Scourge has an active, intelligent spirit inside. This spirit has its own agenda and possesses its own Will which it can use to influence the wielder toward its ends. It grants the skill Wizard Lore to the wielder, which is Lore about wizards. Scourge does not communicate via telepathy or words, but by changes in the blade\u2019s physical state (i.e., temperature, light, weight, etc.). It can also influence the wielder\u2019s body if the wielder does not remain vigilant and firm of will (WIS rolls to determine).

      Instincts for the Spirit:
      \t\u2726\tslay evil magic users or magic users who commit \u201cevil\u201d by the spirit\u2019s standards
      \t\u2726\tslay magical monsters
      \t\u2726\tnot retreat when faced with either of the above

      5) WITCH FINDER.
      Scourge grants the wielder the skill Sense Magic User, which it communicates wordlessly via a physical change in the sword (i.e., temperature, light, weight, etc.).

      So yeah, Scourge might turn out to be ridiculously powerful in actual play, but it's also a testbed for fiddling with variations to WoDu mechanics. I figure the wielder will be plagued in the fiction by the sword's Awakened Spirit and its own goals via regular mental/emotional rolls. But as I read over this, I'm thinking +1 damage to wizard types may be minor compared to the exploding 6 power. If that turns out to be underpowered, I may make that a +1d6 down the line, maybe when the wielder levels up.

      On the other hand, if Scourge turns out to be a vorpal reaper engine of destruction, I'll make the sword's spirit that much more willful and unrelenting. Fun will be had either way.

      Arian had possession of Scourge when the session started, Niff not having been there last time, and G rejecting the blade as another "not paladiny" flavored weapon. I pointed out that Arselan wasn't picking up any signs of evil from it (his goddess wasn't warning him), but G wasn't budging. Skull pommel, she figured, meant bad juju.

      Next: The Bonding of Scourge

      \n I'm not sure if you've talked about this previously, but what are the ages of the characters? When I've played with my kids, they're always creating heroes close to their own age. Just curious how it's manifested for your games.

      \n I like Scourge!

      I feel like it would be extra cool if some of the powers depended or varied based on the current "stored" die.

      When the stored die is low, maybe the spirit inside is hungry and restless.

      When you swap out a 6, the sword makes a psychic scream heard only by the wielder and any magic-users with half a mile.

      When the stored die is a 5 or 6, the blade turns blood-red and glows in the dark.

      Stuff like that.
