      Christopher, the Dungeon Girls all seem to conceive their characters in the 15 to 17 range, from what I recall. Nobody's mentioned specific ages, though. JM has mentioned she sees Mist as about 14, but the younger set doesn't have a good grasp of ages. Everything over 10 seems old to them.

      \nSCOURGE (revised)

      Thanks to Paul for his fantastic ideas on flavorful powers, and to Phil for his nice catch. Ashen Kings is what I'd wanted, but Dust Kings was the first take. Fixed.

      Description: Heavy Masterwork short sword of pale gold metal with black serpents intertwined on the blade, a pommel of garnet worked in the form of a skull

      Owner: Arian Saeth

      POWERS:

      1) ALCHEMICALLY FORGED
      Masterwork weapon forged from orichalcum: 1d6+2 damage, unbreakable by normal means and highly resistant to magic.

      2) FATED WEAPON
      When a new owner picks up Scourge, take a scarlet d6 and set it to \u201c1." Anytime you roll the dice while wielding Scourge, you can swap the scarlet die\u2019s current value for one of your dice. That die\u2019s value becomes Scourge\u2019s new Fated value.

      So if I roll a 4 and a 5 and get 9, I may want to downgrade to a 1 and a 5 and rely on my stat to pass the check (or my skill to keep from failing on a 6-). So you have to suffer a few setbacks to power Scourge up, but then you\u2019ll have a 5 or 6 stored in the sword, waiting for a crucial roll to use it.

      When the player is using Scourge to confront evil magic users and creatures of magic, use Scourge\u2019s die value for the Die of Fate result for things related to the wielder without swapping it!

      When you swap out a 6, the sword utters a psychic scream heard only by the wielder and any magic-users within half a mile.

      When the stored die is a 5 or 6, the blade turns blood-red and glows in the dark. Add the tag messy while the die remains at this level.

      When the stored die is 1 or 2, the sword is morose and irritable. Apply the tag unlucky while the die remains at this level.

      3) DEADLY
      When wielding Scourge, any 6\u2019s rolled to hit for for damage with the sword \u201cexplode,\u201d meaning you keep the six and reroll that die, adding the result to your total. If you swap out the six per FATED WEAPON, you do not reroll at that time, but may reroll at the time you swap in that six.

      4) MAGE KILLER
      Deals +1d6 damage to any character who has a Special Ability from the Wizard class. When Scourge successfully deals the death-blow to a magic user, take +1 forward with the weapon until the next die swap per FATED WEAPON, above. This +1 is cumulative.

      5) AWAKENED SPIRIT
      Scourge has an active, intelligent spirit inside. This spirit has its own agenda and possesses its own Will which it can use to influence the wielder toward its ends. It grants the skill Wizard Lore to the wielder, which is knowledge about wizards based on the spirit\u2019s experience in hunting and killing them. Scourge does not communicate via telepathy or words, but by changes in the blade\u2019s physical state (heat, weight, vibration). It can also influence or even control the wielder\u2019s body if the wielder does not remain vigilant and firm of will (WIS rolls to determine).

      Instincts for the Spirit:
      - slay evil magic users or magic users who commit \u201cevil\u201d by the spirit\u2019s standards, esp. any remaining servants of the evil undead wizards once known as the Ashen Kings
      - slay magical monsters
      - not retreat when faced with either of the above
      - torment its wielder if he or she does not follow the sword\u2019s fated purpose
      - slay whatever hinders it from destroying the servants of the Dust Ashen Kings\u2014or the Dust Ashen Kings themselves, if any survive
      - do not tolerate the wielder using other weapons to accomplish Scourge's fated purpose

      6) WITCH FINDER
      Scourge grants the wielder the skill Sense Magic User, which it communicates wordlessly via a physical change in the sword (i.e., temperature, light, weight, etc.).

      7) BANISHER
      When Scourge does damage to a magician, the wielder may change a stored 6 per FATED WEAPON to a \u20181\u2019 in order to sever a Spirit Mark on the wounded magic user and break that mark\u2019s pact or bond with the allied spirit. The magic user cannot summon that spirit again for a year and a day.

      8) SPIRIT-SHUNNED
      Most spirits do not care for Scourge, considering it arrogant and destructive. They tend to treat the wielder with caution or even dislike. However, spirits of justice, vengeance, or war may be more friendly.

      HISTORY
      Scourge was a weapon forged for use in the struggle against the Ashen Kings, powerful Undead wizard-tyrants who dominated the southern lands hundreds of years ago. In the course of this long war, the sword changed hands many times, but was said to have been wielded at the siege of the Stained City of Durga\u2019alos where it struck down the hideous Ireshkanri, Queen of Maggots, one of the last and most powerful Ashen Kings. With her fall, the other Kings fled. Many were hunted down and slain in later years, but the fates of three were never ascertained.

      When last noted in the scrolls of history, Scourge had been carried into the deep desert by its last known wielder, an eastern barbarian named Nathor, neither to be written of again.

      \n We start the new session with an almost-full deck. Sklarah isn't here since L is still unavailable. M is struggling over Arian's decision whether to bond with Scourge. Meanwhile, I describe how Sklarah (whose player isn't here) backs away with a nervous expression as Arian shows the sword to the party. The wizard (Die of Fate = 4) knows a little about the sword, but not the details of its history. What she does know is that it is a powerful weapon made to kill wizards, used in the ancient wars against the Ashen Kings. She relates how tales of Scourge were told to frighten apprentices into sticking to the Path of Light. Despite her anxiety, she acknowledges the sword isn't said to be evil itself.

      M files that away with an evident mixture of trepidation and excitement. The party splits up the rest of the loot, which includes a mysterious silver-ornamented coffer. Niff (F is here today) (success) easily picks the lock, to reveal a softly glowing pink crystal. The girls immediately break into a clamor of who might get it, but the conclusion that emerges is that pink doesn't work for Andromeda or Niff, and Arselan isn't too thrilled with it either. Arian says she has the sword and doesn't need anything else. It comes down to either Valavanora or Sklarah, but EM is here, and she hasn't taken much lately, so the crystal falls to her.

      Various Lore rolls happen. Valavanora (crit) recognizes the crystal as an Ioun Stone, its pink color indicating its virtue is to fortify the user's CON. When keyed by the owner naming the sigil etched in the stone's heart, it will glow bright pink and swoop in orbit around the user. When the owner speaks the sigil of rest, it will gently settle into the user's outstretched hand.

      EM shrugs. "Cool." The Ioun Stone vanishes into Valavanora's belt pouch.

      M decides Arian will bond with Scourge, though she continues to feel some trepidation. Via Sklarah as a mouthpiece, I tell her major artifacts work a lot like pacting or bonding with spirits, since the Big Things typically hold Awakened Spirits that only grant their full power via pacting. The implications of the skull pommel symbolism is what seems to be throwing her off, but at the same time, it's clear she's intrigued. F makes a few quiet comments indicating his interest, but doesn't press the issue. It's clear Arian is the one in possession.

      The party is a bit nervous about this process, so Andromeda uses her Ritual skill to construct a Prison circle for Scourge and Arian. It's questionable whether a Necromantic circle would work for long against a non-necromantic spirit, but I allow the attempt. If there's a problem, I'll handle it via fictional positioning. So the circle is scribed in an area of the courtyard swept clean of sand by Valavanora's cricket wind spirit, which she summons the long way. This isn't stressful, so I don't bother requiring EM to roll.

      The bonding goes well. Arian (success on WIS) carefully cuts herself on Scourge's blade and lets a few drops of blood fall onto the enameled serpent heads near the tip of the blade. The sword seems to warm in her hand. The garnet skull begins to glow like a coal, and the ranger feels the spirit's presence. Her fingers curl around the hilt without her conscious volition, and she feels her arm rise, the sword pointing in Sklarah's direction.

      "No," Arian says, alarmed. "She's my friend. All the magic users here are my friends. They're not evil!"

      The sword becomes suddenly icy to the touch. After a moment of silent struggle, she (success on WIS) is able to lower her arm and loosen her grip. She feels a sudden, hot pain in her hand, then the sword's temperature returns to normal, neither warm nor cold. The skull pommel's glow fades, but the back of her sword hand now bears a small brand in the shape of a human skull.

      Next: The Merchant of Maggots!

      \n Thanks, Noofy. I'm enjoying it, but I'm seriously behind on this AP. Have to finish the DG, get a DK session in, and there's another DG tomorrow... I'm learning a lot from these kids, making a bunch of mistakes along the way, but overall remain happy with how well things are going. This little game produces an astonishing amount and quality of play for such a small footprint.

      I don't recall if I've talked much about it here, but one of my goals is to provide all the kids a steady habit of geek fun that gives them something to continue to connect with through middle and high school. Social connection paired with creative collaboration.

      \n First, a quick interlude about monkeys. Monkeys are clever, agile, and dextrous. Monkeys ride well on your shoulder. Monkeys are cute, too.

      And this is all relevant how?

      See, from the beginning of Dungeon Girls, the kids in both groups have been interested in acquiring Pets. I've fielded questions about everything from spiders and snakes to dragonets and perspicacious lorises; pets seem to be a big draw for the players. In fact, I'm working up a mini character sheet for pets, since we've got three of them between the two groups. Honestly, the pet obsession has been one of the bigger surprises for me as we started this game.

      But there were monkeys at this bandit spot. Remember the cliff?

      Niff decides he'd like to tame a monkey. The table falls into a discussion of how to lure a monkey down, and what age the monkey should be, etc. F wants a young monkey that can be trained, an intelligent one. A cracks a joke about how he needs to avoid being saddled with an old, dumb specimen. They debate about traps and bait and such, until M points out that Valavanora can just talk to them using her Wild special ability. Everyone quickly agrees this is the way to go.

      And this is all happening concurrently with M having Arian anguish about Scourge, so there was heavy drama struggling to unfold alongside monkey chatter, in essence. Table management with this crowd is sometimes a challenge.

      So Valavanora (partial success on CHA) talks to the monkeys and, acting as an intermediate for Niff, (success on WIS) eventually persuades a young, intelligent-looking monkey to come down and join the group. The deal is for fruit and snacks. Snacks are taken from the bandits' rations to pay off the monkey troupe. The initial offer of food with the partial success had gotten a huge response, with all the monkeys volunteering to join. The second roll noticed the young smart monkey sitting back and pitched the offer to him.

      So the monkey joins the group. As it happens, Junior Moppet is hanging out at home today by herself, and I've been feeling like I haven't spent as much time with her what with the new job, so I ask if she wants to play the monkey. She says yes and joins the table. I scribble down some monkey stats on a 3x5 card and we're off to the races.

      Generally, I try to keep my daughters separated in these groups, so each can enjoy time with their peers without big or little sister energy. Today my inner Dad yielded to include JM. It was kind of an experiment, not a horrible one, but it confirmed that separation of the age groups is the best arrangement for now.

      JM being the dynamic player she is, you see, regarded the monkey as a Heroic Monkey. A protagonist rather than a supporting character.

      This intention, while not a bad idea, would clash with the conception of a cute, occasionally useful monkey pet held by the rest of the group, as we'll see. JM is whip-smart, creative, and damned good at heroics. The monkey would be a source of cognitive dissonance going forward, as it threatened to overshadow the rest of the group.

      Next:\xa0 The Merchant of Maggots for reals! And about the Necessity of Nerfing Monkeys.

      \n Great stuff! (And that's how a magic sword should be handled, oh yeah.)

      I wonder how the monkey caused you trouble? They can be scene-stealers, those monkeys. I remember having some issues with pets and familiars when I was around these kids' age myself.
      \n

      \n
      \n

      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n

      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Monkey business having been completed and the sword bound, the bandits defeated, the party continues on its way across the Great Desert to the coast. Arian (success) leads the group to an oasis after an uneventful three day journey. I have in mind there'd be an encounter, and I draw a Harrow card. It turns out to be The Wanderer, which depicts a Centaur tinker/merchant image.

      The party discovers a tent, a small wagon, and a mule team. All these turn out to be owned by an itinerant merchant who is at first suspicious, but soon warms up after the characters show they meant no harm. The presence of the paladin (CHA Leadership success) goes a long way to reassuring him.

      I don't remember the guy's name, but he was from the Regency and so had a name from that list. No, he wasn't a centaur, though I was tempted. I decided not to interpret the card too literally in this case.

      He sets down his spear and explains he is a wandering merchant who does business with the nomads who roam the Great Desert. The players immediately ask me if he has (a) interesting pets, or (b) cool magical items. Die of Fate is noncommittal, and I say, no, he's a dealer in trinkets, spices, glassware, and jewelry. The party is interested anyway, so they pick through his stuff and haggle a little, trying to sell off some of their objects of art. It quickly becomes evident the party's loot is rich beyond this guy's means. The characters set up their tents and settle in for the night.

      I encourage some in-character RP around the campfire. The kids have been talking about sharing their backstories among the characters, and this moment seems tailor-made for doing so.

      It is pretty cute, honestly. They take turns around the table to tell their stories, a little haltingly, most of them a bit self-conscious as they try to find their characters' voices. A finds her footing pretty quickly, EM and M come off a bit more wobbly but have a lot to say. G portrays Arselan as curt and direct, but confident. F remains curt and mysterious, in part because he hasn't had a chance to develop Niff's backstory yet.

      "Eek, eek," says Junior Moppet after the others finish. "I'm a monkey."

      There follows a more strategic discussion of goals and destinations. They are curious about the Merchant of Maggots from Andromeda's prophetic vision--the name has clearly caught their imaginations. The wandering merchant says he's heard something of the Merchant of Maggots. Evidently, she is a slave dealer and (rumor has it) something of a sorcerer as well.

      When we made the map a few weeks ago, the moppets and I had established a town called Vespa (named after a slave ship from The Roman Mysteries book series) famed for its a notorious slave market. Some characters now think Vespa might be a worthwhile destination, but the consensus is to stick to the goal of the Druid Lands. They wonder how to find out more about the Merchant of Maggots, and this discussion spins out awhile without going anywhere.

      Then the monkey offers a suggestion through Valavanora, a simple idea that cause the other kids to pause and say, "Huh. Yeah. That'd work." I don't remember the suggestion now, but it was definitely one of those odd moments when everyone realizes JM is been paying attention.

      Someone murmurs, "Smart monkey."

      So they go to sleep, setting a watch. Soon, however, they are all asleep, sharing the same dream. In this dream, they're asleep in their camp under the desert stars. A shadowy figures slips into their midst, going from tent to tent, eventually looming over Arian and Hodari, who remain fast asleep. A gnarled hand reaches for Scourge--

      Arian (success on WIS) jolts awake, Scourge so cold in her grip, it practically burns. She struggles out of her blankets and finds the camp empty, with everyone asleep, the fire having died down. Die of Fate makes the watch person Sklarah (for what it's worth). This is a nice group. No one rags on Sklarah, though I suspect if it had been Andromeda or Niff on watch, we'd have had an outbreak of snark. Everyone seems to accept the mysterious figures was the Merchant of Maggots, and that the dream itself was magical.

      But they're awake, and share notes. In a few moments, I call for Awareness or WIS rolls. There's enough success around the table, and I go from low to high with perception results, so that the high roll hears everything everyone else did, but gets an additional snippet of information. The sandy scratchy, clicky noise indicates something huge is sort of slithering, sort of skittering to camp.

      "Ooh!" JM cries. "Purple worm! Is it a purple worm, Daddy?"

      Dammit. The kid knows how I think.

      "It's probably not a purple worm," I answer. "It's probably the desert version of the species."

      "Shai-hulud," A suggests.

      This comment draws blank looks around the table.

      "Sandworm," she clarifies, still not eliciting understanding from her friends.

      "Desert worm!" I exclaim. "And it's dark except for starlight. What are you going to do?"

      Everyone looks at each other.

      "Umm\u2026light torches?" says M.

      Next: Night Worm Fight!

      \n Today's session time is drawing to a close, with parents soon to arrive.\xa0 The worm is approaching, but still distant.\xa0 The party is trying to figure out what to do.\xa0 Andromeda decides to summon one of her necromantic spirits to give the party night vision.\xa0 She swigs some quicksilver and (success) calls one of her allied spirits.\xa0 I don't recall the domain, but it's not a stretch.\xa0 The spirit does as it is commanded, and the entire party plus merchant gain the ability to see in the dark for (die of Fate) four rounds.

      They see the towering figure of the worm as it rises up dramatically to catch sight of its prey.\xa0 JM tells us (referring to the Monster book) the horrid thing is 80 feet long and 4,000 pounds, with a maw big enough to engulf a standing man.\xa0 Delicious.\xa0 Also, it has poison fangs in its huge pincers.\xa0 The way it's drawn, it's more like a monstrous cross between a caterpillar, a beetle, and a tapeworm.\xa0 I describe its mottled bulk as it draws closer, a cluster of eyes arranged over the deadly pincers.

      "How are we gonna kill that?" asks Arian.

      "We need to find a weak spot," says G.

      "Like the dragon in The Hobbit!" A says.

      "I scamper over and grab a kitchen knife from the campfire," says JM in the part of the monkey.\xa0 "I hold it with my tail."

      There's a pause.

      "I don't know," says M.\xa0 "I think\u2026"

      F nods.\xa0 "I don't see a monkey doing that."

      "Not too realistic," EM tells JM with a little of that big sister tone.

      G cuts in, "We need to find a weak spot."

      EM is thinking.\xa0 "Daddy, can my spirit Mir use its Secrets power to find a weak spot?"

      Why not?\xa0 Sure.\xa0 We haven't seen Mir yet.

      So Valavanora takes a dose of quicksilver and summons Mir, her spirit with domains of Water and Secrets.\xa0 Mir manifests, by EM's description, as a misty blue sprite like the ones in Brave.\xa0 Valavanora asks for the secret of the worm's weak spot, and Mir (success) shares the knowledge with the party of a scabbed over spot about a yard wide on (die of FATE for location) the left-hand side of the worm, near the head.

      The party spreads out, hashing out a rough strategy.\xa0 Niff and Arian stay in the middle, near the camp, from where they will shoot arrows at the worm.\xa0 Andromeda and Arselan flank to the worm's left, hoping to hit the weak spot.\xa0 Sklarah stays back too (NPC), and I figure I'll use her for a magic effect if necessary to help out if things go pear-shaped.

      "That's where the monkey goes, too," declares JM.\xa0 "With the kitchen knife in my tail."

      F and G exchange a look. M says, "I don't know about that. A monkey fighting a giant worm?"

      "It's a brave monkey," JM insists.

      The players shrug and conclude their maneuvering. Valavanora flanks to the worm's right, from where she plans to wield her bow and may call on her standby fire spirit Koriander.

      We have time left in the session for a round of arrows (successes) and the monkey scampers up to (critical) whack at the worm's weak spot with the kitchen knife.\xa0 The older players roll their eyes and EM sighs, but I allow the monkey to do an HP of damage anyway. There's not much time left. M's mom has arrived for pickup, so we move to wrap up.

      The consensus seems to be that a PC monkey was over the top, and the kids were pretty direct, though not unkind. They like JM, but the monkey business was breaking their -- for want of a better word -- immersion in the game. Too jarring. It wasn't helping that with JM at the helm, the monkey was shaping up to be freakin' awesome.

      JM, to her credit, took no offense. She's cool with staying out of Dungeon Girl business unless there's an epic Dungeon Kids crossover at some point in the future.

      We left it on one final ominous note: the worm seems to fixate on Arian, its head tracking her movements as it lumbers forward. Cliffhanger!

      Next: Dungeon Kids and the battle with the troll!

      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n

      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n So this week with Dungeon Kids, we have all four kids: the two girls JM and S with their double character stable (Mist and Amber, Rhavaniel and Lostariel), and the boys C and J, who are playing the Imperial dwarf Romrama and the elf archer Ingor respectively. A full house.

      After some time for the kids to play on their own and vent some energy, we gather around the table, naturally arranging themselves with girls on one side, boys on the other.

      Last time on Dungeon Kids, they had defeated the hobgoblin garrison, kept the thing in the chapel contained, and brought the ranger Rhavaniel back from death. Now...the citadel's courtyard is littered with hobgoblin bodies. It is still dark, not yet dawn. The mountain air is chill. The stars gleam like ice crystals overhead.

      "What do you do?" I ask. I'm about to offer suggestions of possible avenues for action and exploration, but J calls out, "Loot the bodies!" The other players take up the cry, and so everyone gets to roll against WIS to see what they find, dividing up the roughly dozen bodies evenly. Everyone succeeds except Ingor, who rolls a partial success. They all find a few silvers on the bodies, but as Ingor stoops to search his third corpse, the hobgoblin twists up, snarling, a dagger in its hand!

      Ingor (partial success) leaps back and avoids the hobgoblin's thrust, but loses his footing on a slippery patch of flagstone. As he goes down, the hobgoblin hauls itself to its feet. Its fur is clotted with blood, and its hateful glare shows neither fear nor mercy.

      Meanwhile, the other members of the party are reacting. Die of Fate rolls for each put most of them far enough away that they can't get there for one or two rounds. Rhavaniel will need a round to pull out her bow. Mist is too far away for a dagger throw and turns out to be the farthest away.

      The hobgoblin raises its bloody muzzle to the night sky and screams out what Ingor and Amber (success) can tell is a prayer-curse to the hobgoblin's gods. It begs for those dark powers to bring vengeance upon the slayers of its kin!

      J asks if he can throw a dagger at it. "Sure," I say.

      "Can I throw my axe?" asks C for Romrama. Yep, he can.

      They both roll. Ingor (crit!) hucks his dagger straight into the creature's throat, and Romrama's axe (success) also strikes true. The hobgoblin goes down in mid-scream, deader than a doornail. The boys bump fists. First blood!

      They're reckoning up their thin gleanings from the hobgoblins when the door to the chapel shudders under a heavy blow from the thing inside. Everyone pauses.

      "I bet that's the curse," S says.

      JM nods. "Yep, it's gonna get out."

      "What is it?" asks Ingor, who missed the last session.

      "We don't know," S says. "But it's bad."

      "We barely kept it in last time," JM adds.

      The door shudders again from another blow, and wood cracks. "HOO," says the thing.

      The party scrambles to take up defensive positions. The suspense is palpable, but the girls seem more curious. The boys are trying to sort out which weapon they want to use. JM tells C he should use the wolf-head maul they'd captured from the bugbear captain. At first, he's not sure, because it's a two-handed weapon, and Romrama loves his shield protection, but the girls talk it up as so cool-looking that he relents. Mist positions her sunstone for light.

      The dwarf takes up a position well off to the side of the splintering door, while the others array themselves facing the door from a reasonable distance, missile weapons at the ready. Mist takes up her elven sword and stands guard in front of Amber.

      A few more blows and "HOOs," and the door's hinges finally give up. The door is smashed outward, the thick boards broken. From the darkened interior of the chapel emerges a filthy greenish figure with a long nose and long, lank hair. It steps out on splay-toed feet, then straightens a little to tower over them in a stoop-shouldered posture, its arms long enough that its taloned fingers drape almost to the flagstones. And it has a carrion smell.

      "Ooh, ooh," JM calls, fidgeting. "Is it a troll, Daddy? Is it?"

      Make a Lore roll, kid.

      Amber (success) recognizes the monster as a troll, and I hand over the Monsters book to JM, who takes it and flips straight to the troll entry, which she proceeds to read aloud to the rest of the group. What stands out for them is that trolls are stupid and hungry, so throw food at them to delay them; they regenerate any damage not caused by fire or acid; and the females are larger and more powerful than the males. This last attribute turns out to be an important one for the group.

      JM pleads, "Can this be a girl troll, Daddy? Pleeeease?"

      The other kids shrug. S decides to back JM's request. Girl power!

      OK, I say. As fate would have it, this thing is a troll-hag with a ragged shift offering an attempt at modesty. What do you know?

      I bump the HP up ten points to 50. Honestly, I don't know if the kids can take this thing, but they've surprised me so many times, I'm willing to push the boundaries a little. There's a good possibility I'm going to beat up on them pretty hard this session. Aside from 50 HP, the troll regenerates Die of Fate HP per round and it has Armor 1. Those black, grimy talons do 2d6 damage. The troll's qualities are Fiendishly Strong, Tireless, Ravenous. Its Instincts are Eat the Living, Tear Stuff Apart to Get at the Chewy Center, and Feel No Pain.

      This is going to be a throwdown.

      Next: The Rumble with Rations!
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

    • \n
      \n

      \n
      \n
      \n\nPaul_T \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Very cool! What/how do you use the "qualities"?
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n I tend to think of the Qualities as roleplaying personality, as opposed to the Instincts, which represent behavioral goals. In that context, the "Feel No Pain" as an Instinct is more about if it does feel pain, it tries to stop or evade the source. Think of "Feel" as an imperative. That may mean fleeing from or destroying the source of pain, depending on circumstances. Certainly it'll go after whatever just hurt it most recently. Kinda awkwardly phrased, but that's what I scribbled down in my all-too-short prep time.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Oh, and if it's Fiendishly Strong, that informs the fictional scope of what it can do, like batter down a thick wooden door with its bare hands, that sort of thing.
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Battle is joined. The troll-hag sniffs the air, says "HOO!" and peers at Ingor and Lostariel with beady eyes. Its mouth splits into a hideous grin and it starts toward them, arms extended.

      I tell JM Amber has heard trolls like the taste of elves better than anything else in the world. "Oh no!" says Ingor. S smiles. She clearly likes this idea.

      "Mist throws some rations at it!" shouts JM.

      Indeed, Mist (success) bounces a ration pack off the troll's forehead. Brow furrowed, the troll looks down and clumsily snatches up the rations and shoves them, wrappers and all, into her snaggletoothed maw. I pantomime exaggerated chewing as the troll is successfully distracted this round.

      Rhavaniel (crit) puts an arrow into the troll's eye, bypassing armor and doing 8 damage. The troll looks up, frowning, then reaches up to pull out the painful arrow. I make icky sound effects and pantomime that as well. This elicits a chorus of "Eww!" from the kids.

      Using a fresh bowstring on his bow, Ingor shoots an arrow that (partial success) hits the troll in the shoulder for 3 HP, doing 2 after armor. Unfortunately, it draws her attention back to the tasty elf meat waiting for her.

      "HOO!" She resumes her advance, still chewing. Die of Fate gives the troll back 4 HP. She's at 44. Her eye scabs over with fresh green tissue.

      "We need fire or acid, guys!" says JM. "Mist throws more rations at it!"

      "Next round, honey. What are the rest of you doing?"

      "Hmm," says J for Ingor. "I have a wand of acid spraying. Would that work? It has five charges."

      I stare at him. Goddamn. I'd forgotten about that. It was a random loot result from that website. "That\u2026would work," I tell them.

      "Ingor puts away his bow and gets out the wand."

      That'll take you this round, I tell him.

      Romrama prepares to hit the troll from the flank as he was standing off to the side. At first, he's going to use his axe (retrieved from the hobgoblin corpse) and protect himself with his shield, but the kids tell him he should use the bugbear's wolf-headed maul. It's a two-handed weapon, and for a moment, he struggles with the prospect of not using his shield. In the end, the wolf-head cool wins over.

      "OK, I'll use the mace," he says. "I take it in both hands and get ready to attack."

      Rhavaniel throws rations this time, and (success) once again catches the troll's attention. The hag squats to eat this little appetizer. Mist moves between the troll and Amber, her elven sword up on guard. Ingor readies his wand.

      The troll (die of Fate = 5) regenerates to 49 HP. Her healing eye reopens with a squelch, messy fluids trickling down her greasy cheek.

      New round. Ingor steps forward and (success on INT to activate the wand) and (success to aim it properly) directs a stream of green vapor from the wand to the troll's chest, where it sizzles madly for (3d6 roll) 11 HP of damage! The troll takes 9 after armor and drops to 40 HP. The hag shrieks and stands, flailing at her smoking chest!

      I note the non-regenerable damage separately, so the troll's max HP is now 41 for purposes of this encounter.

      The kids cheer. The angry troll takes a stride toward Ingor, and now Romrama makes his move. He leaps forward and (partial success) swings the maul into the troll's femur, where it deals out 8 HP with a loud crack of bone. The troll staggers and drops to one knee. Snarling, she backhands the dwarf for 12 HP. Romrama flies backward a good twenty feet and slams into the chapel wall. After his armor and Tough, he still takes 10 damage. The troll is at 34 HP, still with a max of 41.

      I'm about to tell him he's Dazed until next round, but C interrupts me. "Can I be Knocked Out?"

      I blink. "You want to be Out? Sure."

      "Awesome Point!" he crows, and takes a crystal from the resin bowl.

      What are Mist and Amber and Lostariel and Rhavaniel doing? I ask.

      Mist stays on guard. Amber is thinking. Lostariel readies a dagger to throw. Rhavaniel nocks another arrow for the next round. The kids realize they can't just hack this thing down. Their toughest fighter just got swatted down easy-peasy.

      JM tells J he has to use his acid wand. It's their only hope!

      J balks. "I don't want to use it all up!" he says. "It's only got four charges left!"

      "You have to!" says S.

      J shakes his head. "I'm not going to."

      Interesting, I think. I hadn't run into this sort of reaction before. Resource conservation, yes. But J is clearly identifying as an Elf with an Acid Wand. He doesn't want to lose that tag.

      Meanwhile, the round ends, and the troll (die of FATE = 4) straightens its leg and stands with a wet click of knitting bone. Her HP come back up to 38. She snarls.

      What are you doing? I ask the table.

      The kids yell for Ingor to shoot it again with his wand. "Fine," he says. "But just this one time." Ingor levels the wand and (success on both activation and to-hit) blasts it with another dose of acid, this time for a measly 7 HP. the troll is down to 33 overall, and its max is now 36. J finds this a bit disheartening. I describe how the wand sears the troll's shoulder but seems to be a glancing hit, which is why it doesn't do as much damage.

      Rhavaniel (partial success) shoots an arrow right into that freshly seared shoulder, doing 4 damage which leaves the troll at 31. The troll fixates on her and charges to destroy the source of pain!

      Next: A steak through the heart?
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJanuary 2013 \n edited January 2013
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n As the enraged troll begins its charge, Mist leaps in front of the troll and (success) throws a steak at it!

      Waitaminute. "A steak?" I ask.

      "Mist likes to eat well," JM tells me. "It's part of her rations."

      "Awesome Point," says S, handing JM a crystal.

      OK, well\u2026cool. The steak hits the troll in the face, and she stops and catches it, sniffing furiously. She jams the meat into her mouth and closes her eyes in bliss.

      "Can Amber summon a Sleep spirit to put it to sleep?" asks JM.

      "Sure, if you have something nearby that's asleep that can be an anchor for the spirit."

      "Hmm." She thinks about it.

      "There are corpses here," suggests S.

      "They're a bit too asleep," I answer.

      "Romrama is unconscious," JM notes. "Would that work?"

      "I'll stay knocked out!" C offers.

      Yep, that'd work, I tell her. So Amber opens her mind to the Otherworld swigs a dose of quicksilver and calls on a spirit of Sleep this round. It'll manifest next round.

      (I should add here that Amber having gone through her Star of Otherworldly Madness/Mutation last session, her magical warp is that her hair now moves as through constantly windblown, wind or no. All the kids think this is pure awesome. Experienced mages in this world are clearly freaks.)

      Ingor refuses to shoot at first, but the kids prevail on him to zap the troll again with the acid wand. This time, he (success) on activation, but (failure) on aim means the shot goes wide as the troll drops into a low crouch and continues to chew the delicious, delicious steak. Ingor is bummed, not in a bad sport way, but because he doesn't want to tap out his wand. There are two charges left.

      Left unsaid here is that the kids have been burning through the Awesome Points to elevate their die results, so their supply is thin. There's not enough in the party to rescue this wand roll. Also, Ingor has to make an activation roll because he doesn't have Lore. He gets to use the wand at all because he has a Wizard Special Ability. This is, admittedly, a bit of a hacked interpretation, but there you are.

      "Mist takes her sword in both hands. I'm going to cut its arm off!" JM declares.

      "Next round, honey," I tell her.

      Lostariel throws a dagger that does 2 HP to the troll after armor, sticking in the troll's bony scalp. "HOO!" the hag utters, standing again, rage rekindled in her beady black eyes.

      End of round. The hag regenerates (die of FATE = 2) to 31, so this round is a wash, damage-wise.

      New round. The troll lunges toward Lostariel, the last person to deal it damage. Mist steps up and (crit) for 11 points of damage after armor, takes off the hag's left arm arm at the elbow. The troll is down to 20 HP, but all this is regenerable. But the troll howls as her black blood splashes around her. Mist easily tumbles out of reach, sword held high in a cool pose. The troll gnashes her teeth as her severed arm thrashes around on the flagstones.

      Meanwhile, the sleep spirit (crit!) materializes in front of Amber. I gather some evocative details from the kids around the table, and what comes of it is blue smoke, glass, and shadows. JM describes it as a unicorn made of blue smoke and shadow with a glass horn and glass eyes, but if you look at it differently, it's a nightmare. So it's dream one way, nightmare the next.

      Awesome, I think. Wow. The girl continues to surprise me with her raw creativity.

      "What do you wish me to do for you, wizard?" asks the spirit.

      Now, Amber could Command it, but she thinks that's mean, and the crit roll gave her an Awesome Point and the chance to ally with this spirit.

      "I want you to put that troll to sleep!"

      "Is that all?" the spirit asks.

      "Would you like to be my friend?"

      "What would you give me for my service?"

      JM thinks, but only for a second. The troll is moving, after all. "You can take one of my dreams every month!"

      Jesus Christ, yes. The spirit agrees. "On the night of the new moon each month, I will take your dream that night."

      S thinks this is cool, too. "Whoa. You might have this awesome idea or prophecy or something, but then you wouldn't get it because the spirit would take it. That's really awesome."

      The unicorn spirit leans out and its horn traces delicate whorls of tiny words and pictures across Mist's eyelids. "The bargain is sealed, mortal." For a moment, it's the nightmare speaking, its mouth full of shadows.

      The spirit vanishes in a sigh of blue smoke, which moves to the troll. A moment later, the hag (success) shuts her eyes, yawns, and flops down onto the flagstones with a snore. Her arm's stump (die of Fate = 6!) blisters over as a new hand begins to push out. She is back up to 36 HP, her cap after all the acid damage.

      Everyone breathes a sigh of relief. The only problem now is what to do with the troll. She might wake up. She's really strong, and she's regenerating. Rations are low.

      "No more steaks?" S asks JM. JM shakes her head. "Mist only had one."

      They talk about it. J is adamant about not wasting his acid wand charges, but the kids don't have enough to burn at hand, and they're not clear they can get a fire started before the monster wakes.

      "I can cut its head off," Mist says.

      "But then it'll just regenerate," Rhavaniel muses. "Ingor needs to use his acid wand."

      Ingor protests, but he's eventually convinced this is OK so long as he can do so economically enough to keep a charge. They ask me whether, if Mist decapitates the hag quickly, Ingor can sear the head and neck stumps with one charge.

      So long as the head doesn't roll away, I tell them.

      So that's what they do. Mist (success) cuts off the head, and Ingor (success) activates the wand. I don't make him roll to aim, and I don't have him roll damage. This is a smart plan.

      I describe how the troll's eyes open in rage, and her teeth gnash as the acid sears her. The body flops around, the head gnashes until Mist takes her elven sword in both hands and spikes it into the flagstones to keep it still.

      I'm practically standing there with my mouth hanging open at this.

      Romrama stirs and sits up. "What'd I miss?" he asks in a nice bit of RP. "Did we win?"

      "No," S says. "She's eating us!"

      Everybody smiles, even J. He still has one charge in his wand, and his magic enabled them to defeat this thing. It was a real team effort, and I give them all XP and Awesome Points to reinforce the point.

      "Nice job, Dungeon Kids," I say with feeling. "Nice job."

      S asks me if the sun can come up and turn the troll to stone. It's nearly dawn in game time, so I describe how they do their healing and general clean up, and when the sun comes up, Mist pulls her sword free just before the still twitching troll head petrifies with the touch of sunlight.

      "OK, go play," I say, and the kids scatter from the table like puppies. I'm left alone with a table covered in character sheets and glory.

      Next: The Dungeon Girls go EPIC.

      \n What? That wasn't EPIC enough for you?

      Oh, man.

      A question: what's the deal with the fighter being knocked out and taking an Awesome Point? Is there a precedent for that?

      (Quick aside: you were worried--or maybe I was worried--that the way magic works, combined with the pentagram, makes magic-working characters too powerful. How's that working out? I mean, it doesn't sound like having your hair constantly moving as though wind was blowing and stuff like that is *all that* scary. It could even desirable! What are your thoughts on this?)

      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n

      \n
      \n Hey Paul,

      OMG, trust me. The Dungeon Girls session we had this last weekend blew my socks off. I don't know if it'll impress the readers here, but...yeah. I'll just have to write it up. The girls (and Niff) are taking it to the next level.

      Romrama volunteered to be knocked out. I've told them they can volunteer for nontrivial consequences to get Awesome Points. He did so without prompting and was perfectly happy with that. In fact, it worked out great, given Amber's idea of calling a sleep spirit.

      Regarding the "Opening your mind to the Otherworld" move to bypass quicksilver, I was worried at first, but I made it clear to JM that it's a spiral. The first time you fill up the star, it's just weird, but not harmful or terribly inconvenient. The second time, it's somewhat inconvenient, but not harmful or grotesque. The third time, it's groteque. The fourth time, it's harmful in some way. Past that, each subsequent filling of the star piles on the serious. She seems to be taking the cautionary note to heart. And...as I write this, I'm looking over my notes and finding out she'd actually taken quicksilver after all.

      Anyway, I'm not worried about it anymore. I told the DG the same thing about escalation: weird, inconvenient, grotesque, harmful. They don't mind weird or inconvenient, but grotesque and harmful definitely have them worried.

      \n

      \n
      \n
      \n We left the Dungeon Girls (and Niff) facing the attack of a giant desert worm (desert variant of the purple worm). The purple worm is more like a giant caterpillar with beetle pincers, huge, with a maw big enough to swallow a standing man.

      Our player call today is four, since Elder Moppet is down with the flu and girl L is out of state. We've relocated to G's house, a pleasant, light-filled open space with a larger table. Snacks are abundant, as G's mom is a great host. G's dad is graciously watching the football playoffs in another room. G, M, A, and F gather around the table.

      We've upgraded to the new character sheets I posted earlier in this thread. The kids like them and seem to appreciate the clarity.

      When I came up with this encounter, I decided to hit them with a beast. To date, everything the players have fought has been in the realm of 1 to 15 HP. The worm has 75 HP and 3 armor. Its Qualities (descriptors) are Massive, Gross, and Immune to Mental Effects. Its Instincts are Eat Everything, Get Scourge First, and Swallow or Crush. It does 3d6 damage, with a chance of swallowing its prey if said prey fails an Escape the Maw roll. Since I haven't thrown anything like this at them, I have no idea how hard this will be to take down, but I'm envisioning a serious contest.

      So the worm is approaching, its massive bulk slithering over the sandy terrain, the first quarter of its body rearing up. The party has a few rounds of night vision bestowed on them by Andromeda's spirit. Valavanora's spirit Mir had identified a weak spot on the worm's left, not too far from the head. This is a scabby network of scar tissue unprotected by the worm's thick mottled hide. The monkey has been shrieking and running back and forth trying to stab the spot with a kitchen knife, but now it scampers away. The merchant at the camp has fled in terror on a mule, leaving his wagon and goods behind.

      The characters had scrambled to come up with a strategy. The general position has Arselan, and Andromeda flanking the worm's left, trying for a shot at the weak spot. Niff and Arian hold the center. Valavanora is flanking on the worm's right. They'd had a round of arrow volleys for a meager total of 5 damage, knocking the worm down to 70 HP as we start the combat.

      The worm seems to be making for Arian, who is trying to decide between her masterwork bow and Scourge. At last she decides to try out the sword of power, though reluctantly. Its Fated Weapon number is 1, which means the sword's spirit is sullen and bestows the tag of unlucky on Arian.

      The worm charges!

      Arselan runs up to the weak spot, plants himself, and taking his masterwork sword in both hands, hews at the weak spot. G describes how the paladin is using the worm's momentum to add to the force of his blow, and I tell her that's worth a +1 bonus to damage. His blade (critical!) slices through the worm's weak spot (no armor) practically to the hilt, opening a long, deep cut for 24 HP of damage! Green gore spills out of the wound. I describe the shhhliik! sound the sword makes. Everyone is impressed.

      Here's how I've been handling combat crits. Generally, if a critter has HP less than or equal to the normal max damage of the player, and no special abilities or immunities apply, a crit gives an insta-kill or a kill with style if it's more of a coup de grace situation (1 or 2 HP left, for example). Depending on circumstances, I may allow a situational advantage or hold going forward. Otherwise, I double the total damage. So Arselan rolled 12 HP of damage (masterwork longsword for 1d6+2, +3 STR, +1 damage bonus) that doubled.

      The worm is dumped to 46 HP. Jesus.

      Andromeda the Necromancer is up next, since I'm going clockwise around the table. She steps up with her longsword in one hand, swings at Arselan's cut and (critical!) delivers an additional 12 HP to the worm that opens up that gaping wound even more. The monster is down to 34 HP already, and we're only halfway through the round.

      Niff is up next as the worm charges Arian. He (success) hurls a frost globe from the Skitterlings, aiming for the mouth. He hits a pincer and does 10 HP of cold, bypassing armor and immobilizing the right pincer for fictional positioning purposes. The worm is at 24.

      Valavanora shoots another arrow, since EM had told me last session she wants to conserve spirit use for a bit. She's an NPC today, so I just roll the damage: 5 HP. After subtracting the 3 Armor, the worm is down to 22 HP.

      What does Arian do? I ask. Leap aside and take a cut or leap into the maw of the worm and strike at the frozen part of the mouth? You might bypass armor if you do that, I add, trying to lure her in to the pincers and their poisonous barbs.

      M hesitates. "I don't know. Probably leap aside..."

      This elicits a chorus of "Go inside! Do the mouth! Go for it!"

      After a moment, she sighs. "All right. I'll probably regret this, but\u2026I leap inside and use Scourge to hack at the frozen part."

      Arian boldly leaps inside, swings Scourge at the pincer, and\u2026rolls a 6 and a 4. Scourge's Deadly power means 6's explode. I tell her to keep the six and roll an additional die. She does so and\u2026rolls a 6. She keeps that and rolls another 6 and then a 1, for a total to-hit well into crit territory.

      Arian has STR of +1, so her initial roll isn't a crit. Good as it is, Scourge doesn't come with a to-hit bonus. However, the first die explosion gets the crit, and the second one\u2026hmm.

      Having played Ars Magica and dealt with exploding crits on rolls of 1, I decide each crit 6 earns another crit. I don't know if I'll keep that, since it seems utterly deadly. But I'll try it out for now.

      She rolls 3 damage, which yields a total of 6 after her STR and sword bonuses factor in. 6 doubles to 12, which doubles again to 24, which hits the worm in a spot with no armor and obliterates its remaining HP.

      I describe how Scourge cuts into the worm at the point where the pincer joins to the head and how despite the blade's modest length, it delivers a twenty foot cut that shears off half the worm's head in a slimy SSHHHKT of green gore. Empowered by her stellar critical, Arian lands safely without being hit by the caustic blood, landing in a relatively clean area of sandy ground. The worm collapses, dead as dirt. Its insides leak out of the hideous wounds and spread upon the starlit ground. The caterpillar legs make one final spasm and shift the worm forward about ten feet. Then it lies still.

      The party is quiet. M looks a little stunned.

      Andromeda breaks the silence. "Woo hoo! We did it!"

      "I don't know if I like this sword," M murmurs. I picture Arian staring at the sword in her hand, overcome by foreboding.

      "I'll be happy to take it off your hands," Niff says.

      "No, that's all right. I'll hold onto it for now."

      I'm sitting here thinking, "Holy cats, they freakin' clotheslined that thing in one round, and it was only really two-thirds of the party engaged. And they did it all the old-fashioned way: with steel."

      I'm gonna need a bigger boat monster.

      Next: How to Loot a Worm, and a Clash of Alignment

      \nWell, yeah, play would be different, but I think the good sportsmanship with the Dungeon Girls/Kids has far more to do with the GM and the players than the rules of the game in this case. World of Dungeons doesn't really have any rules that encourage good sportsmanship. It's a product created at the table, not in the text.

      EDIT: Although if you want to file Blake's Awesome Points and "you can't die unless you want to die" house rules under "system matters", I suppose those two things would encourage the good sportsmanship. That's a blurry line though. I'd personally file that under "GM matters".

      \n Thanks, guys. Both groups of kids are mature for their respective ages, at least as far as cooperative play goes. I've been trying to model the sportsmanship factor by showing lots of appreciation of their actions and offering as much transparency with my agenda as possible, but it's an easy sell.

      For example, their unselfish use of Awesome Points to help one another wasn't something I suggested, but emerged organically from their own negotiation. It quickly became a group custom, very natural, unquestioned. Likewise their evenhanded split of items, XP, and treasure. It's sort of evolved into a natural creative socialism at the table. There was no discussion around it, just a question to me if they could do it in the first place. Once I said yes, the practice took off.

      System obviously matters, too. The mechanics are streamlined, yet produce rich results at the table. We're not spending time consulting tables or trying to figure out esoteric rules. In-game conflict moments resolve quickly and intuitively, with lots of room for creative leverage. Even with this group, I suspect a crunchy system like any edition of D&D past the first would have slowed things down a lot and put up fences around the free-ranging creativity I've seen with these groups.

      EDITED to add: For this play genre, Dungeon World would very likely work with these kids, maybe 13th Age.

      I've thought about how they'd do with something like the upcoming FATE Accelerated, Lady Blackbird, or Wushu. They all (well, the moppets and their besties) say they like WoDu better than Faery's Tale, in part because WoDu and the AW-DW core mechanic map so well to clear fictional results. EM also thinks the high fantasy backdrop is easier to engage with than a faery forest.

      \n Well, there the party stands in the aftermath of this punk-ass worm slaughter. Their magically enhanced sight gives them a clear picture as they assess the gigantic corpse. Their sense of triumph is interrupted as Niff asks whether the worm's hide is worth anything.

      "It's pretty thick hide, right?"

      Yeah, I say. 3 Armor's worth.

      "Great. How much money?"

      I don't know, I answer. You'll have to haggle over that, but it's sure not something common.

      F nods. "It's probably worth getting some and selling it. I'm going to get out my sword and start cutting off some hide."

      "Ooh, me too!" says A. "And I want to get some of the poison sacs from the mandibles."

      The other characters follow suit, right down to the paladin. Within moments, they have pivoted from fighting a monster to reducing it to parts.

      Don't waste any part of the monster, a little stunned voice in my head whispers.

      "How much can we get?" asks F. I give a rough estimate as they all roll STR to see how much worm hide they can flay off the massive corpse. Their night vision expires, and they produce torches and lanterns from their supplies, their characters continuing their practical butchery.

      "You could write a book on how to dress a worm," I quip.

      "Hey," A says, "I could summon a spirit and make a huge zombie of this thing. Wouldn't that be awesome?"

      Yes, I say. Awesome is one way to describe it.

      "Gross," says Arian's player, M.

      Arselan nods agreement. "That sounds sort of evil to me."

      "Oh, come on," says A. "It'd be cool! And if any of you die, I could bring you back as zombies! Just think how great it would be to have a zombie army with a giant undead worm!" She goes on to wax enthusiastic about zombies and especially the zombie worm. The other players don't think it's a good idea and are growing a little antsy as A continues to be carried away by her idea.

      I decide to have a little fun of my own. "Hey, is Andromeda saying this stuff out loud for reals?"

      A shoots me a quizzical look. "Huh? What do you mean?"

      "Are you saying this zombie and undead army stuff out loud?"

      "Why?"

      I jerk my chin at M. "Someone," I say, "someone might have half-drawn a certain sword without being aware of doing so. Its garnet pommel might be pulsing deep red, like a coal."

      A pauses, her mouth open. "Ah. No. No, I'm not saying any of this out loud." She proceeds to change the topic away from zombie creation toward how she's going to dig poison sacs out of the mandibles. And can she find the worm's brain?

      M's lips curve in a little smile. "I think I'm starting to like this sword."

      The characters proceed to work through the night, until each of them has a couple of yards of rolled and tied worm hide. A has recovered some poison from the pincers. It's at this point conversation turns to the merchant's wagon. Andromeda starts looking through it for glassware to store the poison she's harvested. Debate springs up around whether the party is entitled to take what they want without payment.

      Andromeda and Niff fall on the side of "the merchant bugged out and abandoned us, so this is all ours."

      Arselan takes the position of "it's not ours, and we shouldn't take anything without paying a fair price."

      Arian wavers at first, but comes down on Arselan's side. Stalemate among the day's players. The arguments pretty much follow iterations of the summaries above. Eventually, the Lawful position wins. Arselan makes the point that they have plenty of gold, and the merchant wasn't a bad guy. They decide to have Valavanora send her peregrine falcon familiar to carry a message to the merchant and guide him back. Then they take what they want and set aside some funds from their coin to pay for it. All this comes from roleplaying. The only die rolls in this section are about how much hide they can whack off in the time they have available.

      M does not use Scourge for this bloody task, as she gets the vibe from it that such work is beneath a Sword of Power.

      When the merchant eventually returns, he is enormously grateful and gives them the glassware for a token price. Niff asks for cinnamon, I think because he has some idea of making a cinnamon bomb, and they buy out the merchant's stock. Everybody's happy, even Andromeda, because even though she didn't' get a zombie worm or free loot from the merchant's wagon, she has worm poison and a roll of bloody hide that represents extra silvers when they get to the next town.

      After some deliberation, they decide to head to the coast and take ship for Ankhyra. Arselan wants to be on the water, and several kids (including Valavanora in outside conversations I've had with Elder Moppet) are eager to fight pirates on the high seas. Hmm, I dunno. Flag, anyone?

      Next: The gates of the port of Durat-Zur
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nFebruary 2013 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nMan, I'm so behind on this. After I get caught up on this episode, I think I'll have to stick to highlights. My apologies for taking so long.

      So continuing the current session, the party arrives at the city of Durat-Zur, a port on the inner sea (name TBA). I describe a city a bit like Tangiers, surrounded by high rose-colored walls, irrigated fields and orchards. The characters approach a gate that appears heavily defended, with guards checking everyone entering the city.

      At this point, I have nothing prepped, so I take out the CITY tables from the random tables I'd downloaded from Story Games. Rolls produce the result (and I paraphrase) "The nobility is playing games." So I figure the guards are searching people and harassing outsiders.

      Andromeda tries to talk to the guards and (failure) causes them to deny the party entry. This result throws the party for a loop. As I continue to roll on the CITY table, I come up with a monster result that reads like "They seek to enslave." I flash to a concept that the entire city has been taken over by a mind-controlling monster\u2026sort of like a miniature version of the zombie apocalypse.

      Mind-flayers. Oh yeah. And inspired by The Wrath of Khan, they are doing it via some sort of brain parasite administered through drinking water. OK, now I have a plan.

      Arselan steps up and (partial success) persuades the guards to reconsider. They do so, but are only willing to admit the paladin, and only if he leaves his weapons behind. After a brief consult with the other players, G agrees. Arselan hands his weapons to Niff and begins to lead his warhorse through the shaded arch of the gatehouse.

      At this point, I ask Arian to roll WIS. M does so, and (success since she has Awareness) receives a secret note in the form of a folded 3x5 card from me. The note reads, "You notice the guards seem unusually stiff and glassy-eyed, carrying their duties with flat expressions."

      A, seated next to M, immediately wants to know what the note says.

      "Arian, do you share your observation with Andromeda?" I ask.

      "OK, I guess, sure." M leans over and opens the card so A can read it. They whisper excitedly.

      I pitch my voice to carry and tell G, "Arselan, as you enter the city, your warhorse clopping behind you, the guard captain approaches you with a silver goblet in his calloused hands, saying, 'Greetings, honored paladin. The masters of the city bid you accept the drink of friendship."

      A and M freak out, and begin howling at G. "NO! ARSELAN! Don't drink! Don't take the goblet!" Let me be clear: by "freak out," I mean full on, squealing, standing and bouncing up and down hysteria. They are losing it in a thoroughly awesome way. I'm a little nonplussed, honestly. See, A is very dramatic and prone to excitement, so her reaction isn't a surprise. M, however, has been very measured and thoughtful in her RP to this point. But here they both are, going nuts and shouting over each other, clearly caught up in this sweet, sweet moment of suspense. I guess it's the equivalent of "you see the zombie shuffling up behind your friend, but your friend doesn't" kind of thing.

      I can't stop laughing, not just because of the girls' reaction, but because G's expression shows she's completely baffled. She gestures at A and M, perfectly portraying Arselan's confusion as he raises his hands to beckon for a clearer explanation. The two girls continue to shriek delightedly and shake their heads at G.

      "DON'T DRINK!" they shout. "DON'T DO IT!"

      G exchanges a look with F, who shakes his head. He's equally lost, but tells me Niff produces one of his lightning guns and takes aim at the cup.

      The guard captain holds the cup closer. "Drink, traveler, from the cup, and join us in friendship."

      After a moment, Arselan shakes his head. "Thank you, but I will drink later."

      Two guards on either side of Arselan seize him and the guard captain grabs the paladin by the jaw and raises the silver cup. "You will drink, traveler. You will be a friend of the masters." Arselan tries to free himself, but (failure) the guards hold him fast. The girls' hysteria hits a new crescendo.

      The girls are still shrieking when Niff fires the lightning gun and (success) blows the goblet out of the guard captain's hand, the discharge branding the hand in the process. Arselan (success) shakes off the guards at last and whistles for his warhorse, who begins to wheel and kick, clearing the area. Niff runs under the arch to back up Arselan as more guards begin to emerge from the towers, moving in eerie, coordinated silence. Behind them, civilians in the street near the gatehouse also begin to turn and approach the gate, their faces blank.

      From the top of the guardhouse, a bunch of guards appear with bows in hand and prepare to loose a volley at the party. Nunk moans in terror. Not more arrows!

      \n Arrows are loosed at the Dungeon Girls! Nunk, unfortunately, takes several and drops to one knee. Valavanora (an NPC here) takes a slug of quicksilver and calls on her fire spirit Koriander to burn the bowstrings of the guards, a stunt the spirit is getting good enough at for me to consider boosting the effect at some point in the near future. The Druid and Sklarah hunker next to Nunk and try to help him. Since Valavanora has the Heal skill now, that seems an appropriate thing to do.

      Scourge in hand, Arian uses her frog ring to leap atop the battlement and avoid the arrows, but she (partial success) misjudges her leap and lands with precarious footing while the guards cast aside their bows aside and draw short swords. One of them (die of Fate = greater than 1 for her "unlucky" tag) grabs her by her free arm. Her lion Hodari evades harm by springing into the gatehouse and mauling a guard.

      Arselan (success) grapples with the guard captain and throws him against the wall, stunning him. Niff (crit!) charges in, avoiding the stubby grabby efforts of the intervening guards, and throws the paladin the weapons Niff had been holding for him. Then he unlimbers his +2 Kite Shield and shoves back an incoming guard while the warhorse wheels and kicks. Add the mighty fierce lion, and it's Pandemonium under the archway.

      Andromeda (success) uses her Necklace of Mouse Size to shrink to the size of a mouse and dodge the arrows that way. Once small, she skitters aside, weaving through other confused travelers to get to a place farther down the wall where she can enact a Summoning.

      The other players shift nervously when they hear Andromeda is going to summon something. "Is that really the best idea?" M asks.

      A says, "Of course!" Or words to that effect. A sigh passes around the table, and several heads shake. Necromancy, you know?

      "I can't see any good coming from this," murmurs F.

      Andromeda returns to full size, takes a deep breath and opens her mind to the Otherworld to begin the summoning of\u2026what, exactly?

      "A spirit of possession so I can free the city."

      That would be a HUGE spirit, I say. You'll be able to free 3d6 worth of guards unless you summon something really, really big. Which would, I say with relish, be dangerous.

      She pauses before answering, "I think I'll go with a regular spirit."

      It has to be a Necromantic spirit, I caution. Something to do with Death, the Dead, Decay, or Darkness.

      "How about Worms?" she asks.

      Worms is good. We like worms. So Andromeda begins her summoning. She doesn't have a Name, but the presence of the possessed guards and citizenry qualify as an example of the domain she seeks. Using bone dust from her pouch and a stick to scratch out a hasty circle, she starts her ritual.

      Arselan (success) lays hands on the guard captain and uses Cure to free him of the mind flayer's control. This works because the guard coughs out a small, red, squid-like creature about the size of a plum. The guard shudders as his volition returns to him, and Niff (success) manages to fend off a pair of oncoming guards. Arselan whistles for his warhorse.

      Up on top of the battlement, Arian (partial success) regains her balance and slams Scourge into a guard. She keeps her partial success even though she opts to put one of her dice showing a 5 into the sword per the FATED WEAPON power. Scourge glows coal red and drops the tag "unlucky" for "messy." The guard frowns as blood pours from his severed arm. The guard who has hold of her other arm, however, pulls her down and the other guards (there are nine in all, close in, trying to grapple.

      Meanwhile, a shadow opens in Andromeda's impromptu circle. Through it rises a grotesque marionette held on shadowy strings. Its body and head are made of writhing worms.

      "What service do you wish me to render upon you, Necromancer?" it intones. I rasp up my voice for this, somewhere between Christopher Walken and Gollum.

      "Free the possessed people in the city!" Andromeda asks.

      "That is beyond my power," I remind her through the spirit. "I can perhaps cut the strings on a score, but no more."

      Then\u2026hmm. Andromeda thinks about it, as A opens a discussion about who she should try to free. The players start talking about tactical priorities, and I have the other players go through a roll. NPC wise, Valavanora calls upon Koriander again to create a ring of fire to keep her, Sklarah, and Nunk safe while things are going down.

      Under the gate, Arselan (success) leaps astride his horse and cuts a dashing figure as the horse slams through the guards into the city proper. Niff (success) blocks a couple of spears with his shield and pulls his lightning gun. On the other side of the gate, he (success on Awareness) sees a formidable-looking cloaked figure in white scale armor approaching from the stable, holding what appear to be matching wheel lock pistols in each gauntleted hand.

      "Want," says F, reaching for the dice. "I'm going to blast him with my lightning gun."

      Better be quick, I tell him. Guy's drawing a bead on Arselan, who (success) leans down to grab a guard by the face and (success) Cure him.

      Atop the battlement, Arian is in trouble as (failure) the guards work in eerie synchronization to seize her by the arms and slam her against the crenellation. One of them smashes her sword hand against the stone for a few HP. She feels bone crack, but Scourge will not let her release her grip.

      Meanwhile, the side talk that has been swirling around all this has Andromeda bargaining to free most of the guards on the battlement and as many of the guards in the gatehouse as possible.

      "What do you want in return for this?" she asks the spirit.

      The spirit's mouth splits in a horrible wormy grin. "A day of your life, to be given in one of the next four days."

      "Oh, bad idea, bad id-eee-aa\u2026" is the general consensus around the table.

      Andromeda doesn't care much for this. "Uhm...how about twelve hours?"

      The spirit chuckles, and I ham this up with phlegm. "I accept...if my time begins immediately."

      Andromeda hesitates, clearly not comfortable with this notion. "What will you do with my body?"

      "Oh, simply enjoy the many delights of corporeal existence." The spirit's worms writhe a little faster.

      "Do you promise not to hurt anyone while you're in my body?" Andromeda asks. "I don't want any of my friends hurt. Or innocent people."

      "Perhaps," the spirit says. "Do you wish to extend my time?"

      "Not really. How about--"

      At this point, I tell Arian: "The guards force you down against the crenellation. One guard approaches with his sword held high as he readies himself to cut off your hand, still holding Scourge in a painful grip--"

      M's voice rises in agitation. "HELP!"

      "Do it!" Someone says, I don't remember whether it was F or G.

      Andromeda grimaces. "Done."

      \n Andromeda rolls for the spirit's effort and gets 16 as the result. A describes how Andromeda feels a sensation of falling backward into a deep well of darkness and wakes in a narrow, dank room with two small windows set next to the high ceiling, suggestive of eyes.

      It's clear she could sit out the session, so I wonder about alternatives and inspiration strikes. Andromeda falls again into darkness and blinks. She is in a different body lurching toward Arselan and Niff from the city side. She gets right away what's going on.

      "Please don't let me be a dude, please don't let me be a dude\u2026," A mutters to herself.

      Die of FATE says\u2026"You're a dude."

      "Aww, man!" she covers her face and shakes her head in mock despair. M and G laugh. It's all in good fun, but they are digging this.

      "Oh my gosh," M says. "You're a guy!"

      "I'm\u2026a\u2026dude," A whimpers. "Goh!" She pleads for me not to tell my daughter, to which I answer with an evil laugh.

      It turns out (die of FATE) Andromeda's occupying the body of a tall, young, muscular guy, maybe a kind of smith with his bare arms.

      Oh. Well, that's not so bad, she allows, perking up. "At least I'm a burly guy. I can bust heads!"

      There is that.

      "Where's my body?" she asks.

      Oh, I say, waving airily. Somewhere out there, beneath the big blue sky.

      She gives her head a little shake. "Oboy. NOT good."

      But then she shouts at Arselan, "Hey, Arselan! It's me! Andromeda!" and proceeds (success) to bust heads of nearby civilians.

      G does a great job of roleplaying Arselan's reaction. "Andromeda?"

      Meanwhile, Arian is free. One guard is still under the influence, while the others are reeling and puking out their controllers. She doesn't want to kill him, so she (success) strikes with the flat of the blade. Unfortunately, Scourge is charged and glowing and messy, so she breaks the guy's nose and face, causing blood to spray and the guy to start screaming as the blow to the head (maybe with the sword's influence) causes him to puke out the mind control critter.

      M sighs. This sword\u2026

      "I need my hand healed," she reminds the group.

      Down at the gatehouse, Niff fires his lightning gun at the mysterious gun-wielder and (crit!) nails him in the chest with a perfectly placed bolt. Because it's a crit, he gets his shot off before the other, and does a good amount of damage. The lightning lifts the guy off his feet and hurls him back a good fifteen feet through the stable door with a crash of wood, leaving wisps of smoke trailing in his wake.

      "Yesss!" F does a reverse fist pump, elbow at his belly. "Got him!"

      As he starts for the stable, he gets into a brangle with a couple of townsfolk trying to grapple him. He fights them off, but it's tricky. One of them is a kid, and he tries not to deal out too much damage.

      Arselan (success) makes a Leadership roll to rally the newly liberated troops, then jumps off his horse. While Andromeda the Dude runs interference with the civilians trying to attack, he lays hands on two people to try a double Cure.

      He fails, but I seize the opportunity since we're close to the end of the session. In Arselan's mind, his goddess Ceridwen appears. "I will grant you the boon you seek, but you must prove yourself by undertaking a task for me."

      "I will," Arselan says without hesitation. "Anything."

      The goddess smiles. "Free the city."

      She vanishes. G's eyes widen.

      The two people are cured, and I narrate the camera pulling back high over the gatehouse so we see the oncoming crowd filling the main street from the gatehouse all the way to the docks, as the population of the entire city begins to rush toward the gate, the lead elements breaking into a run, eyes wide, froth coming from their mouths. They are several thousand strong, at least.

      \n Thanks, Myles. I'm hoping the gaming bug sticks so that when they're adults, they'll have so many epic war stories these will be far, far down on the stack.

      John, that's a good idea, thankya. I've been using 3x5 cards and am giving the Pets truncated stats, skills, and special abilities, and putting the onus on the player to run them.

      Paul, that's a really good question. None of them like to miss sessions, but if one or two can't come, we've soldiered on anyway in the interests of logistical continuity. But we're actually dealing with that in a different way tomorrow, as G can't make it. She's asked us to delay the story so Arselan can participate. I'd left them on the brink of an epic confrontation with the mind flayers and a bunch of their allies and a party of controlled adventurers. G was hoping for a delay because this quest is such a big deal for the paladin "to show what he can do," in her words. I said yes, and M was curious about why the exception. But nobody seems to be out of sorts. This group is awesome in sportsmanship. I don't know if it's a girl thing, to be honest. They're definitely more mature than I was at their age.

      So we're going to set up an alternate party using World of Planarchs. This'll work well anyway, as A was talking about swapping out Andromeda and playing Fox for awhile. With the older girls, an alternate group might be the way to go, and EM has been talking about converting her Faery's Tale character Shadowlock into WoDu anyway. Fox will probably end up being a half-fox spirit, half humanoid breed. I am looking forward to it--Planarch Girls!

      \n Heh, I wish. Still trying to catch up with both groups, and then there was today's Planarch session, which was mostly chargen, but ended up with some nice scenes. I could damn near make a part-time job out of playing and logging these kids' adventures.

      The Dungeon Girls really liked the more open-ended style of Planarchs, in which it looks like the racial heritages may play a bit like FATE aspects. It was interesting to see what they came up with. They're also starting to discuss how to run their own games, as A in particular would love to play every week. Elder Moppet suggested that any of them could learn to be a GM, but thought G and A would be particularly well-suited. Poor A is over for a sleepover and pining to "dungeon." Unfortunately, the moppets are more into social time just now than gaming.

      And not to divert from the main narratives, but today we launched the new party with a half-Kitsune, half-Mechano-angel mechano-warrior (A), a Shadow-sprite survivor (S), a Demonic demon-hunter (F), a Stormblooded Elven witch (L), and a Draconic alchemist-wizard (M). That's a lot of hyphenated characters. Borrowing from an awesome idea thread elsewhere on SG, they're a Special Errands Patrol for the Dis Planarchic Library. Their first gig is to retrieve a particular scroll from the Far Elastrian Stacks, Row of the Brazen Oak, about an hour's travel from Main Desk Plaza. The patron who made the request looks ominous, hooded and dark, with bolts of magical energy playing around his shadowed face. Whew!
