      \n Dungeon Kids! Edited to fix some things after actually reading my notes from last session and talking with the kids at the start of today's session.

      We have a full house again in the aftermath of the epic troll battle. Now the kids are mopping up and exploring the citadel, for which I have printed off a pre-gen map gleaned from the internets. I have one thing in mind for today's session, mostly because I haven't had any time to prep: there's an orc wizard still at large in the keep, but he's (wisely) not going to come out into the open to be summarily whacked. He has a Darkness-Poison spirit, a powerful Charm-Passage Demon, a Fire-Wolf spirit, and a Brutal-Stone spirit in his magical quiver. The idea is to throw out some stealthy spirit attacks and see how the kids do with a cat and mouse game, but keep the Stone spirit and Fire spirit for more direct assaults. And I have also placed some loot. Otherwise the plan is to riff off the kids' actions. That's worked pretty well so far. The orc is in the central keep in a locked room where he's drawn his magical summoning circle and is currently pulling in the Demon, who looks like those old D&D half-snake women with multiple arms. Part of my notion is to hit the players with something that looks more like a Disney princess than a traditional monster and see how they react.

      The kids do some exploring, searching for loot. The boys take Romrama and Ingor to sift through the wrecked furniture and offal of the troll's lair, while the girls head toward the inner courtyard with their four characters, where they split again into Mist and Rhavaniel on the one hand, Amber and Lostariel on the other.

      The kids are really squirrelly today, and it's hard to keep them on task, especially when they've split into two groups. My patience is tested as I have to remind them more than a few times to quiet down so I can hear what the acting pair is saying. This is an unavoidable piece of working with younger kids. The older Dungeon Girls also need reminders from time to time, but not like the little ones. I can't help but feel a bit like a Grinch, though.

      I did take the time to place the loot at a few locations on the map, but the girls come to a larger building on the map that looks like a great hall or a large stable. Lostariel listens, while Amber waits nearby. Meanwhile, Mist and Rhavaniel enter the main keep, which requires them to access an upper door placed midway up the wall like a sally port. They are headed toward the orc wizard's sanctum.

      The boys resolutely refuse any hints that the troll's lair doesn't have anything worthwhile, and continue to dig through piles or wrecked furniture, etc. In retrospect, I was too literal about the little prep I did. I should have tossed in something for them to fight or loot. I did have them make a couple of STR rolls to shift heavier bits of rubbish, but that's hardly exciting. This counts as a Failure on my part. Soon they decide to head over to join the girls.

      Meanwhile the Amber/Lostariel pair arrive at the stable. A WIS check (partial success) determines they hear something scratching inside. I don't really know what's in there, but scratching seems interesting. I'm curious to hear what they think about it--

      "Another Frost Worm," JM declares with certainty.

      "Ooh, that'd be cool!" says S. "We could make a pet out of it!"

      JM nods. "The book says people ride Frost Worms. We could ride it!"

      A claps her hands. "That'd be so cool!"

      "Plus they're so cute!" JM adds.

      "Having a Frost Worm as a pet would be awesome," C says.

      I'm thinking, "A pet Frost Worm?" The illustration shows a chalk white nightmare, a gigantic cross between a centipede and a maggot. Cute?

      My daughter is odd.

      But I'm going with it, where I wasn't as flexible with the boys. Sure. It's an awesome idea, not the usual thing you hear from adventuring parties. When Romrama and Ingor arrive, the characters slip the bolt, look inside, and see\u2026there's a frost worm in there, alright, a smaller one about 15 feet long. I describe it wheeling around to fix its multiple red insectoid eyes on them and hiss.

      "Probably the baby of the one we killed." JM shakes her head. "It's probably lonely."

      "We have to make friends with it," S muses. "Maybe it would like some food?"

      "We're out of steaks."

      "Would it like some rations?"

      OK, I cut in. What are you going to do, Amber? Lostariel? Ingor? Romrama?

      JM says, "It's probably sad it lost its mommy."

      Amber Romrama walks up to the thing as it rushes up and raises its front half to loom over him, pincers quivering. Amber The dwarf reaches out and (crit on a CHA roll) successfully befriends the damn thing. It lowers itself as he rubs its hide over one eye. S claps in delight. A new pet!

      Everyone is impressed. "Cool!" C says.

      J nods enthusiastically. "Can we ride it?"

      "First we have to feed it and name it," says JM. "But everybody will get a chance to ride it."

      C agrees.

      Next: Naming the Worm, More Orcish Skulduggery, and Mist in Stealth Mode

      \n Thanks, Noofy. I finally read my notes and talked with the kids, and so have some edits for the above piece. Apologies, I left out quite a bit. It was Romrama who befriended the worm, and I got Amber's sleep-nightmare spirit's name confused with Valavanora's kind cricket spirit. *sigh* That'll teach me to write from memory nearly two weeks after the session...

      My hasty prep for the session included drawing three cards from the Paizo Harrow Deck: The Liar, The Crows, and The Sickness. The first depicts a beautiful serpentine Naga woman, the second three crow-like thieves playing a game, and a plague victim cum zombie.

      When I wrote the last stretch, I neglected to mention that Amber chose to multi-class as a Cleric when she leveled up to Level 3, and she is now a servant of the Goddess of Travelers, the Moon, and Hope. At the start of the session, she takes Cure for her new Special Ability and promptly prays to her goddess for guidance. The goddess (Crit!) answers. Amber asks for help in destroying the castle.

      "You will find a way," says the goddess. "Build me a new temple free of the evil of this place."

      "OK," says Amber. "I will."

      "Then you have my blessing in that undertaking." +1 Forward to actions going toward rebuilding the temple.

      "Thanks," says Amber. "Will you bless our water for us?"

      The goddess smiles. "I will. And I leave you this warning. Beware the crows. And the liar." She vanishes after blessing Amber's waterskin, turning the contents into holy water.

      Back to the current continuity...

      After some quick discussion, the kids decide to name the worm Rattlebeetle. They proceed to feed it some of their dwindling rations, which it scarfs up quickly.

      Mist and Rhavaniel enter the keep stealthily, though Rhavaniel does so with only partial success, and Mist rolls a crit. They enter a vaulted room, at the other end of which they see a door, ajar with green light spilling around the edges. They cross and Mist opens the door and slips inside, still riding her critical success. Meanwhile, dark tentacles unfurl from the ceiling and coil around Rhavaniel!

      Inside the door is a circular chamber, also vaulted. The orc wizard is here, performing a ritual with a great summoning circle painted onto the floor. The green light comes from a pair of braziers blazing with arcane flames. I expected Mist to draw her Elven sword and go to town, but JM has a little smile on her face as she describes how Mist hangs back in the shadows to observe. I asked her later why she didn't simply cut him down, and she replied, "Mist wanted to see what he was doing."

      Meanwhile, Rhavaniel is being pulled toward a circular maw filled with fangs that resemble wasp stingers. She pulls out her bow and (success) launches an arrow into the thing, apparently without effect. As it hauls her closer, she (success on DEX) drops the bow and pulls out her magical hunting spear in time to jam it into the maw and resist being drawn closer this round. The spear does damage, but not enough to banish the spirit. Rhavaniel's panther Madeleine circles frantically from below, unable to leap high enough to help. Rhavaniel cries out for help, and (crit) gets the attention of the others outside. Ingor, Lostariel, and Amber rush into the keep, while Romrama stays outside to guard the young Frost Worm, whom he has named Rattlebeetle.

      Mist continues to watch the orc wizard. In the summoning circle appears a half-woman, half-serpent demon. You know the type: six arms, long hair, beautiful and deadly. I describe the shimmering scales and the lazy, hissing voice as the demon and sorcerer exchange greetings. The orc says, "I command you to..."

      Finally, Mist acts. She holds up her sword and grates, "I think that's a bad idea," in her best Batman voice. She wants to make a CHA attack to intimidate, so she rolls a partial success. The orc freezes and looks over his shoulder, afraid. The sword Causes Fear, however, and the sorcerer freaks out, breaking the summoning circle. The demon is released! She utters a contemptuous laugh and fixes her hypnotic gaze on Mist, who (Failure) fails to resist--

      "I have Lucky, Daddy!" JM says. "I get to reroll!"

      Damn it, so she does. This time, perhaps distracted by the blue light emanating from her sword, Mist (Success) tears her gaze from the demon's. The demon turns and sweeps out of the room, coils rasping on the floor, free and unbound.

      The frightened orc swigs quicksilver and cries out for his Fire Wolf spirit. A wolf made of crimson flames appears and launches itself at Mist in a blaze of fury! I mime how the orc points desperately at Mist, hand shaking.

      JM doesn't faze easily. Mist charges the wolf, holding the Sword of Tirendel in a two-handed grip. "Mist is going to chop that wolf spirit in half, Daddy!"

      I'm so proud. OK, honey, you go for it.

      Mist leaps at the wolf and (Crit!--without Awesome Points, I might add) sweeps her sword through it in one mighty blow, dissipating the wolf in a burst of fire and landing unharmed a few steps away from the orc wizard, wisps of smoke trailing off her sleeves. JM promptly jumps up to show off Mist's awesome victory pose. I'm astonished--again--at her brute luck and nearly pitch-perfect sense of drama.

      "That's so cool," says C. I think we all agree.

      Next: More Spirit Fighting, a Four-Pack of Zombies, and Negotiating with Crows.

    [World of Dungeons] Dungeon Girls!

    \n
    \xab123456\xbb

      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n

      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMarch 2013 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Dungeon Girls! We last left them facing a city of possessed people, with Andromeda the Necromancer having had her spirit dumped into the body of a citizen while the possession spirit she'd summoned goes on a walkabout with her body. Arselan the Paladin has been charged by his goddess Ceridwen to free the city. The entire populace of the city seems bent on destroying them, and we start the session with this World War Z moment of onrushing, blank-eyed crowds.

      Today we are missing M, who can't make it, so Arian and Scourge will be a bit in the background. L and Elder Moppet are here, though, so we have a full complement of magic users.

      Arian (an NPC this session) calls to them from her position on the wall, from where she can see the full extent of the danger. The rest of the characters quickly head for the stair to join the ranger, accompanied by the score or so of guardsmen freed by Arselan and Andromeda. There's some brief talk about running out the gate, but they conclude they can't shut the gate in time anyway. So it's the wall. Arselan's warhorse is there too, along with Hodari the lion and Dera the falcon. The monkey is somewhere outside the wall, but nobody is too concerned about him.

      After looking at the city map and asking the guards for advice, the party decides to make for the temple of Uru, a large, walled temple complex at the SE side of the city. They start running along the wall, and the crowd starts in pursuit, but they're bottlenecked by the stair, so a number of the possessed citizens run through the streets parallel to the wall, a mob that tries to scale the wall when the players pause, and that starts up any stairs it encounters on the way. Meanwhile, the pursuers on the wall are strung out far enough back to give the characters a decent lead.

      The characters are flagging a bit from exertion, though everyone's made their CON rolls to this point. Andromeda pauses, and A asks me if she can still work Necromancy in this body.

      "Sure," I answer, grinning. "Want to summon something?"

      "No," Arselan declares. "No spirits." It reminds me of Darth Vader's line to Boba Fett: "No disintegrations."

      "But\u2026" A affects a pout. "I'm just trying to--"

      "NO." G is adamant. "Every time--every time!--you summon something, something goes wrong. The last thing we need is more necromancy."

      "OK\u2026!" A sighs and they party runs a bit longer, but the crowd is on the wall behind them now and closing, the citizens frothing as the force controlling them pushes them to their physical limits.j

      Andromeda stops again. "That's it! I'm doing something. Can I summon my spirit of Decay?"

      "No, stop!" Arselan says. "NO NECROMANCY!"

      "We have to do something," A argues.

      I roll a 4 on the Die of Fate and put the die on the table. "You have four rounds--less than half a minute--before the crowd reaches you.

      Arselan lines up the guards to make a shield wall, but the guards are freaked. Arselan employes (success) Leadership to firm up their morale. "Try not to kill anyone," he concludes.

      Andromeda calls her ghost--whose name I can't remember right now. Since this is an allied spirit, she doesn't have to bargain. She has the spirit decay a stretch of wall between the party and their pursuit.

      "Hold it," G says. "Arselan doesn't want anyone killed. It's not their fault they're possessed."

      "Not many people will be killed, but we have to do something," Andromeda counters.

      "No killing," Arselan says, playing the paladin to the hilt.

      "I can't guarantee no one will be killed."

      I've ticked the countdown die down to 2 during this exchange.

      "You have to make amends, then," says Arselan. "If anyone's killed."

      A rolls her eyes. "Fine. I'll make amends. I'll serve the city until I've paid them back for anyone who dies because of me."

      Tick countdown to 1.

      "Swear?" says Arselan.

      "Yes!" With that, Andromeda unleashes her spirit and rolls boxcars for effect.

      Tick to zero. The first wave of the pursuers slam into the guards, but they are hurled back, one guard falling off the wall in the process, to be torn apart by the crowd surging around below. I describe how the people in the street are piling up against the wall, squirming over each other to try to climb up and reach the characters.

      Adding Andromeda's INT to her FX roll of 12 for the spirit, something I'm trying out on marginal effect or damage boosts for spirit FX, I figure the effect covers a fifteen foot section of wall. I describe how the stone turns a sickly gray and collapses into a pebbly sludge, tearing away loose stones in its wake to spread it out another few feet. It takes a bunch of the mind-controlled with it, and other runners blindly plunge into it without heed, until the controlling entity appears to take notice. The wall pursuers draw to a halt and stare across the gap at the players, chests heaving, foam flecking their mouths. A few collapse from exhaustion.

      As a post-script, the slurry of decayed stone buries another dozen or more people in the street below. An eerie silence falls over the scene except for the occasional stray pebble falling.

      "Ohhh yeahhh, I'm doing penance." A sighs. Everyone around the table stifles hilarity.

      "Told you," G says. "Necromancy."

      "Come on!" says Niff. "Let's get moving!"

      Next: Temples and Tunnels!

      \n Cool. Penance will be interesting, no doubt.

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nHexabolic \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMarch 2013 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n No doubt. What I really liked about this bit was how easily the girls fell into character and made their moral debate feel natural. It's a classic argument I've seen in a ton of games over the years, but it was fun to see it pop up in this group, all fresh and new for them.

      Niff was pretty much "let the chips fall where they may," but the rest of the group has gotten a bit gunshy (bowshy?) about necromancy, given A's proclivity for dramatic bargains and, y'know, necromancy. Put another way, they've come to the notion that such dark magics inevitably bring collateral damage. I love this.

The plan is to get Dungeon Girls running again so we can bring the campaign to a decent concluding point.
